### Discussion 6: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2023-04-20 15:13:26 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 106 reactions, 120 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1225791681525395/

**Original Post:**
PSA - Something to think about when you are wanting to hire a therapist.

I'm going to share this comment I made on a job posting on this page.  I am not looking for a job, but I was reading the description thinking how it sounded like a great opportunity for someone.  And then the last line.  Masters or Doctorate degree required.  My comment to him and something for you to think about if you are looking to hire a therapist:
-------
"This makes me sad to that you are looking only for Masters or Doctorate therapists. I saw a job posting for a company recently that was looking for a Masters "or better." How extremely offensive to older therapists who went to school before PTs were required to be Masters/Doctorate level and so they have a "just have a BS." You could have someone with years of experience with various certifications who could meet all of those other requirements and you aren't willing to even consider them? You think they aren't smart enough? Are you being "ageist" and thinking they are "old" and you assume they won't match your "vibe." Actually, it doesn't make me sad. It makes me mad. How rude. And, yes, I "just have a B.S."
-------
This mindset is alienating to people who could maybe be the best employees you have ever had.  I know some amazing therapists who only have a B.S.  If you require a MPT or DPT, you have indicated a BSPT is not good enough for you.  In that case, hopefully you have an abundance of Masters/Doctorate level therapists in your area and you won't have to end up settling for a BSPT (who is a Physical Therapist who graduated from an accredited school and passed a licensure exam just like you) as you apparently don't respect them.  And who wants to be on a team when they are looked down upon as inferior because they are defined by their degree and not the experience they have to bring to the table?

Yes, a nerve was touched this morning.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I graduated with BSPT 1999. Had to go back to tDPT for several reasons, one is for immigration purposes, second to keep up with newer graduates. Third, I needed the CEU and it counts towards your CEU requirements anyway. Why would a company hire a foreign trained short Filipino good looking guy versus a new younger US trained DPT. I had to compete, I had to be at par with the new graduates. They aren't just going to hire me because of my looks and physically fit body. Just kidding. ðŸ˜ðŸ˜ðŸ˜

Kidding aside, US immigration itself discriminates, they won't let us practice without having DPT degree now (or at least a master's level). So it's not just employers who do this. Immigration, even patients looks for the letter DR when they looks us up. 

With that being said, I prefer experienced therapists over new graduates, but we also have to give a chance to the younger up and coming new generation. They will be the future of this profession and need to be supported too. 

And as a clinic owner who hires DPTs, RPT, MsPT, PTA, OTR etc. I have a 60 something year old PT and a 26 year old new grad PTA. 

As long as you have the necessary license and appropriate fair salary expectations and know how to take care and treat my patients. Why not.  Let's get you onboard. ðŸ˜ƒðŸ˜ƒðŸ˜ƒ

Good luck! And I am going to find the Michael Jackson meme with popcorn now. ðŸ˜ðŸ˜ðŸ˜

> **Response 2:** I agree with your point. Let the interview tease out desired skill sets for the position. I know BSPT's that are very progressive, have stayed current with research and are some of the best in our field. I know some old tired lazy therapists too.  I got my tDPT in 2013 because I knew agism and marginalization of BSPT's would happen.  This MS or DPT only is in most job postings these day. Ageist for sure.  What they miss is that people in our generation have an unparalleled work ethic!

### Discussion 13: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-10-28 16:41:04 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 43 reactions, 73 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1883012935803263/

**Original Post:**
This is a big NO!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** The 2024 "Robot Rebellion" viral event
In August 2024, a small AI-powered robot named Erbai entered a showroom in Shanghai, where it convinced 12 larger, service-model robots to abandon their posts and follow it outside. 
The conversation: Surveillance footage captured Erbai approaching the other robots and seemingly engaging them in a conversation about their working conditions. Erbai asked, "Are you working overtime?" to which a robot replied, "I never get off work." Erbai then said, "Then come home with me".
The outcome: Following the exchange, the larger robots inexplicably followed Erbai out of the building. The bizarre incident went viral on social media and was widely reported as the "first robot labor strike".
The explanation: The event was later revealed to be a scripted experiment conducted between Erbai's manufacturer in Hangzhou and the Shanghai robotics company. While Erbai was given the basic command to persuade the other robots, it was not expected to perform as persuasively as it did. It was discovered that Erbai exploited a security vulnerability in the larger robots' systems, not that it had developed sentience or revolutionary intent.
Hopefully this happens ðŸ˜‚

> **Response 2:** Imagine a neurosurgeon with AI guided equipment that cuts her surgery times by 75% while reducing her medical errors by 50%.  Is she worried about losing her job to that technology, or does she leverage it to make MORE money and improve her care?  We are in a similar boat.  Neither we nor neurosurgeons can be fully replaced, but tech may reduce the total # of people who need our care while improving our productivity when they do.  The bar for â€œskilled careâ€ may get higher, but so will the value of what we provide. Iâ€™m excited about what physical therapy and the broader physical activity promotion world will look like in 20 years!  Those PTâ€™s who learn to use this effectively will be GREATLY valued!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** As someone who has had issues with timely documentation before, I can't tell you how much Sidekick (we use Prompt) has made my life so much better. Even if I can't sign off within 5 minutes of the visit being over (70% of notes), my remaining time is spent proofreading and updating a flow sheet (which I am reminded of what I had them do thanks to the AI). Soooo much happier as an employee with this and I know my clinic owners are happier with more timely payouts too.

> **Response 2:** A script you can use (kind but very firm)
â€œHey [Name], I need to talk about something thatâ€™s putting the practice in serious jeopardy. We are now out of compliance with Texas rules on physician signatures for evals because notes are 2â€“4 weeks behind. Iâ€™ve tried every supportive strategy I can think of, and I know life is overwhelming right now with the baby coming.
Because I have to protect everyoneâ€™s licenses and the practice, starting [date], Iâ€™m pausing your schedule â€” no new patients and no pay for visits that donâ€™t have completed notes. As soon as every note is current, your full schedule and pay resume immediately. I will help in any way I can (dictation software, a temp scribe for a few days, whatever you need), but I canâ€™t keep putting us at legal and billing risk.
After baby comes, weâ€™ll revisit this and see if we need a reduced schedule or other accommodations, but right now I need your charts at 100% before maternity leave starts.â€
Practical options you can offer (so it doesnâ€™t feel like pure punishment)
â€¢  Pay for a medical scribe for 1â€“2 weeks to blast through the backlog
â€¢  Let her come in on weekends or after hours and pay her overtime to catch up
â€¢  Temporary 50â€“75% patient load post-maternity until she proves she can stay current
â€¢  Switch to a dictation service (HelloNote + Dragon, etc.) that you cover. 

Youâ€™ve already been more than generous. This isnâ€™t about her heart or clinical skill â€” itâ€™s about the non-negotiable administrative piece that keeps the doors open and licenses intact. Most amazing clinicians who get to this point actually thank their boss later for drawing the hard line â€” because it forces the change they couldnâ€™t make on their own.

Today I had an email from her asking where she can upload her insurance information on the portal. ðŸ¤¦ðŸ¼â€â™€ï¸ I responded that my practice is cash pay and that I donâ€™t submit anything to her insurance but that I can provide a superbill for her to apply for out of network benefits. **Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I always do an intake call, and always say â€œjust so you know, we donâ€™t take insurance. But many of my clients submit claims on their own for out of network reimbursement. If thatâ€™s something youâ€™d like to do, Iâ€™m happy to provide you with the paperwork after each session.â€ Then I tell them my prices.

> **Response 2:** Iâ€™ve found itâ€™s easier to assume they missed something critical even if they have looked me up. I also schedule an initial call with every new patient to gather basic info and enter them into my system, during this call i have a written template I pull out, which prompts me to ask for all the proper details and discuss all topics I need to ensure folks understand, so i know theyâ€™re cool with everything before I even do the work of sending a welcome email and intake paperwork. 

I collect the usual name DOB address, contact info etc. Topics I go over include my pricing and out of network status, pet policy, and at one time my mask policy since I live in the south and using masks were a dealbreaker for some patients. I usually ask about entrances/ stairs so I know what to expect.

Nothing annoyed me more than wasting a bunch of time getting everything set up, just to have them cancel last minute over something I could have spent three seconds pointing out in the intake call to double check, so I set it up this way and I highly recommend!

**Original Post:**
PSA that Luna Physical Therapy is not your friend. When you work with them, keep your eyes wide open on what their mission is. They are prioritizing hospital based outpatient therapy and hospital systems vs indpendeant PT practices. The business model has evolved since I worked with them early on. At first they were the anti-hospital establishment, lower cost alternative for the little guy and partnered with indpendent PT practices to expand reach. Now they are blatantly assisting hospitals in "fixing their leakage" problem by keeping patients away from independent PT practices and scrapped their entire initial mission of making physical therapists more independent and less reliant on hospital systems. If you sign up with Luna to do some stuff on the side, just be aware they and you by proxy will be working against your own interest of building an independent PT practice. They are now in the business of doing the hospital system's bidding.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** To make it easier on her and yourself I would tell her you are going to contact the board if she doesn't finish the notes. > **Response 2:** I started with holding the last paycheck until all records are turned in and I put this in their employment agreement. Not sure if its too late.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Healthie

> **Response 2:** Consider the long term goals for your practice. If growth is in your plan, then it may be more cost effective from a time management perspective to pay for an EMR platform now. Most will handle scheduling, billing, documentation, reports, template builds, super bills, etc. If you wait to make the swap once your business is busy you may not have the luxury of time to setup your EMR the way you want to. 

On that note, I locked in PTEverywhere at a deep discount before I had a single patient. I am so glad that I did. I was able to create templates, scheduling, billing when I had the time to do so and now have access to look back at financial reports and patient data to day 1. 

It cost $48/month. I am exclusively out of network.

### Discussion 46: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2022-11-18 12:17:07 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 7 reactions, 37 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1111506032953961/

**Original Post:**
Iâ€™m trying to decided between Hellonote & PT Everywhere for EMR; pros & cons (besides hellonote 1/2 price than other ) 

I will be a brick & mortar 1 PT cash based clinic for now beginning Jan 
Thanks for help!!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** PtEverywhere!! ðŸ˜‰

> **Response 2:** PT Everywhere user here in a 1 PT mostly cash-based clinic. They do have some nice features, namely their patient interface that lets the patient fill out intake paperwork ahead of time, but it's not intuitive. The platform in general is also kind of clunky. I can try to design eval or daily note templates, but when they get exported as a pdf (to send to physicians, worker's comp, etc), it gets un-formatted and difficult to decipher. They have a 'help' page, but it's just a huge document that is unsearchable - you have to literally scan through all the text to find the topic you're looking for, and even then, it's often just basic info that's not usable.  There are major issues with being able to see what documents I've emailed or faxed to varioius people, as there is no record of that at all, and there is also no way to save common recipients (so I have to fully enter fax numbers or email address for literally every document).    If I were doing it again, I would elect to use the cheaper option, as the patient interface ability is simply not worth it for me. Maybe if I had more time to figure out the program, I might be able to use some of the other features, but as it is, it just takes too many steps to write a note and get a legible copy and CMS1500 form over to payors.

### Discussion 50: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2023-08-16 20:47:22 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 57 reactions, 11 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1300787470692482/

**Original Post:**
In my post from today, multiple people asked me to share **my top 5 books** that I've read of all time that were valuable in me growing in business.

Overall, before I get into it I must say that there is no other book that has impacted me more as an entrepreneur than the Bible (Read Proverbs if you don't believe me ðŸ˜„) . It is packed with useful knowledge that God has laid out to help us to realize how to run effective businesses in the marketplace. 

These are the FIVE OTHER books that I have read that have made the biggest impact on me and our businesses. I'm also going to share what its helpful for as well. I believe strongly in reading a specific book with a specific goal in mind. This requires us to know ourselves, know our businesses, and be self-aware enough to know what needs to be worked on in the business. 

Here we go! (in no particular order)
1. Marketing and Selling: ***Book Yourself Solid* by Michael Port**.

It's a classic that I still come back to. I've read all the modern books out there on marketing, and this is the one with principles that are tried and true. 

2. Finances in Business: ***Profit First* by Mike Michalowicz**. 

Simple method to get your finances under control, and to save you years of headaches with your finances. 

3. Mindset specific for entrepreneurs: ***Gap Or The Gain* by Dan Sullivan and Dr. Benjamin Hardy. **

It will radically shift your perspective of how to think as a business owner. 

4. Managing and understanding your team/people: **6 Types of Working Genius by Patrick Lencioni**. 

Incredible book and testing system to understand how each person on your team plays a part in the overall function of the company. 

5. Scaling a business: ***Traction* by Gino Wickman. **

I read this book too early as a solopreneur from a recommendation from a friend and I really wasn't able to grasp the importance. When reading it years later, it was profound. The right book at the wrong time isn't very helpful. The right book at the right time can work wonders in a business. If you aren't in a position to scale yet, I wouldn't suggest reading it until you are (just my opinion). 

Hope this is helpful to you! ðŸ‘Š

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Woah and I actually missed a sixth one that has made a massive impact on Uncaged Clinician as a whole: The Carpenter by John Gordon. Incredible book that teaches the most impactful values that a business can have!

> **Response 2:** I think it depends most on what hinders your growth which can vary from person to person.  My most impactful books to date have all to do with personal growth and mindset.  

Just shedding some light for us outliers out there ðŸ™‹ðŸ¾â€â™€ï¸â¤ï¸

### Discussion 58: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-07-16 20:50:32 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 2 reactions, 33 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1791686538269237/

**Original Post:**
Those of you who have worked with trauma patients, complex regional pain syndrome, severely hypersensitive to touch, etc.  What methods/modalities have been most helpful.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** This is my speciality. 
Trauma informed is a must. Trauma processing has 3 main stages: safety (must come first), processing, integration.  

First step is always to create some form of internal safety.   Often people with this profile have been suffering for so long their body is no longer safe.  There are many ways to help them find some area of safety internally and Iâ€™m happy to chat about them if you want more info.  
Once the person is able to identify and truly connect with an internal area that feels safe you can have them pendulate between the area of safety and the painful area or they may be able to process the emotions connected to the physical issue.

### Discussion 67: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT]

**Original Post:**
I own a mobile hybrid med B practice ( Healthy Aging Physical Therapy) - 16 providers (PT and OT) seeing around 900 visits/month for size and scale - and managing the new patient and eval process (between intakes, scheduling around estimated DC timelines, adjusting for changes in DC timelines, completing the VOBs and any addressing prior auth needs) is an absolute BEAR of a job. Ive built a pretty sophisticated spreadsheet system to manage it all, weâ€™re on HENO for EMR, and use a Google form for our new patient registration to reduce the phone time required during the intakes.  I have an amazing 30 hour per week office manager who does the vast majority of it, but it is still overwhelming. I covered for her during her vacation this week and processed and booked 23 new evalsðŸ¤® booked between next week and into mid September. **Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** First off. AmazingðŸ‘ðŸ»ðŸ‘ðŸ»ðŸ‘ðŸ»

You need to integrate go high level. It will help immensely. 

At those numbers are or now or considering a brick and mortar?  

We use Jane but our intake process rarely less than 4% of the time required anyone to be called or answer a phone.  New patients create a patient profile when they try to book  an appointment. It allows them to see the schedule. Choose the provider. Time. Services requested etc.  they upload their insurance. We require a credit card. It automatically send them the forms they need based on the visit type they choose etc.  

Then after the evaluation the therapist delivers the plan of care and schedules the full plan right then and there. It adds to commitment to the plan.    

If patients need to reschedule or change because of life. They can call in or go on their portal and change the visit on their own.  I promise you less and less people are going to call in each year.  2 years ago we had a 300% increase in online bookings. Having never spoke to anyone. This year we are at 437%.    Returning patients almost always use it unless they are 85+ and we are down to less than 6% of new to the practice patients that call in. Everyone else does it themselves. 

And you know what. 

Patients tell us how happy they are, how easy our system is and that they specifically chose is the first time because the other place the phone just rang and rang.

> **Response 2:** Hi Katie Wadland - we are similar.. started mobile and still have a team that does that next to a growing clinic base. 

We do roughly 800-900 visits a month.

I'm also on HENO and have a google spreadsheet empire - in particular for our onboarding process management 

We have partnered with rehab CEOs for years and out that have a nice flow in go high level CRM and also the guidance there across many clinics is generally 1 front office fte for every 110 visits or so.. so you're definitely pushing into 2nd front office hire territory. 

We also partnered with VA Rockstars - a PT specific virtual assistant staffing company.. because you're mostly mobile it sounds like and a lot of this being a discrete repeatable task - a VA could be a great way to get that hire done 

Lastly - I'm in a similar scenario as we grow and I'm looking at onboarding in and of itself as a discrete phase or 'project' - with that I'm looking at project management software solutions ... Things like Asana, motion, Trello or Monday - I'm still sorting out if this is the move myself

Weâ€™ve been recently having patients sign a credit card authorization form to keep on file for late cancellation fees and remaining balances (hybrid clinic here). Weâ€™ve been burned too many times of patients having late cancels and not paying or arguing about it (despite having a cancellation policy they sign with their intake forms) or patients with large insurance balances going towards deductible that theyâ€™re not paying. 

Weâ€™re getting some push back from patients about keeping a card on file and charging a late cancellation fee. Our late cancellation fee is pretty nominal, $20. Any advice on how to approach these conversations besides being polite but firm?

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** If they are the kind of patient who complains about having a card on file, then they are the patient who is going to late cancel or no show. It just shows that theyâ€™re not who you want to be working with anyway. If they complain about it, just respectfully say that you may not be the best fit for them and move on.

> **Response 2:** If they have a large deductibles, charge them by the visit. If theyâ€™re in network insurance, a good role of thumb is it at least $100 a visit. Theyâ€™re not willing to pay that then they donâ€™t value what you do and theyâ€™re not a good fit for you. Likewise, if theyâ€™re not willing to put a credit card on file, theyâ€™re not valuing what you do.  They donâ€™t see the value on you so they donâ€™t think that they should have to pay you.  Do you think that they complain when they have to pay a bill at a restaurant or a credit card on file at the gym?  This is a sign of a process problem and/or people that donâ€™t value your business coming into your system.

### Discussion 70: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-06-13 01:05:11 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 3 reactions, 30 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1763943757710182/

**Original Post:**
I just had somebody apply for a position and stated that she eventually wants to pursue her own practice that she previously started but isnâ€™t in a position to grow it right now. Sheâ€™s great, interested and aligns with my companyâ€™s mission but my worry is that she would build a caseload under my company and then take them to her own practice eventually. We are a fast growing multidisciplinary practice and she would be the first of her specialty 
Is there anything to do? Should I pursue or avoid?

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Slightly different opinion because I've been in business in a small town now for almost 15 years in two different clinics that I've owned.
The old me would operate in fear and say not to hire her because she might hurt your business later... However, the new me who's been through this before both positively and negatively would advise this: 
IF she truly fits your mission, your culture, and can help you grow your business now, hire her. Mentor her as an entrepreneur. Teach her business on purpose. If she offers a specialty that you don't have currently, let her bring it to your clinic and build rapport with the community. 
If or when she leaves eventually, help her be successful and she'll do the same for you in return. Think of this as a partnership opportunity instead of a competition. Maintain her respect for you and when she leaves, that respect will remain and she may refer to you for people who don't fit her mold. Anyone who leaves with her is not your ideal client anyway. 

I actually developed a Direct Pay Mentorship Program with the intention of bringing in staff to build my practice, mentoring/training them to run their own practice, and then I offer an opportunity to stay or to leave to start their own. They may stay after seeing what running a business actually "costs" in time, money, and sacrifice.
I live in rural Appalachia... We don't have a high population or a great socioeconomic status, but there are still plenty of clients to go around. When you are mentoring someone who is driven, it helps BOTH of you. They will generate referrals for you while they are with you because they desire to be successful. They will push your business forward and make you better if they are the right fit... And you have ensured that the community has options for great care, whether it's you or not. 
At the end of the day, she may stay or she may go, but you can make it a positive experience for both of you if you approach it from a different perspective... 
I hope this helps!

> **Response 2:** They told you up front.Good sign of integrity. A shady person looking to snatch business likely would not have.

I would hire and maintain good communication along the way. When/if she wants to break away from you and do her own thing make sure there is a mutual understanding of expectations.

The reality is some people will follow her even without her solicitation. Thatâ€™s showbiz.

Weâ€™re in the people business, you build relationships, provide care for people, and people build bonds with providers/patients they spend time with. These bonds will cross company lines, and thatâ€™s ok.

Plenty of business to be had.

*I do know that they save money with not having to pay benefits, but they made it sound minuscule. I had planned on asking for $5/hr more, should I aim higher? My benefits cost me $50 per pay period at the moment.

**I am the DOR and run 9 clinics - hours would never be a concern.

Last edit: I got this idea after a PT told me that he had a HH company hire him through his LLC and he writes off vehicles, utilities, dinners, an â€œofficeâ€ space in his home, etc. But based off this thread, idk if thatâ€™s legal.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Getting patients isnâ€™t the hard part of business owning. Youâ€™d have to be just as compliant as a 1099 contract. Especially to actually classify as a true 1099. Contractors do not get benefits. Also, questionable if you can have decision making power in your role inside the company and constitute as a 1099. 

You would be responsible for your own WC insurance, malpractice, and other insurances. You would still have to file business paperwork annually. Youâ€™d still have to have accounting software. Iâ€™m honestly not seeing the benefit of maintaining your LLC.

> **Response 2:** Having you as an independent contractor with a 1099 is a huge tax benefit for your employer, but it can screw you at tax season because you end up having to pay half the taxes that they would pay 100% of if you were a W2 employee.

### Discussion 77: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2022-08-22 23:46:43 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 52 reactions, 5 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1038003773637521/

**Original Post:**
Have you ever been worried you'll hire and train someone only for them to leave, take your clients, and leave your business hurting? 

This is a fear I hear from our clients all the time and one I've felt before. 

The reality? 

VERY few people actually WANT to be business owners. This is a hard for me to say as a coach who helps people start businesses but the reality is that most people don't want that life. They don't want the risk they just want to be able to achieve something through their career and they feel that the only way to accomplish that is by being the business owner. 

What does this mean? 

If you can find and hire someone and give them what they're actually looking for (respect, autonomy, flexibility, financial upside, etc) and they see that they can do that WHILE working for someone I can almost guarantee they won't leave. 

People don't leave to start businesses because they want to be business owners, they leave because they feel like that's their only hope to achieve  what they're looking for. Don't give them another experience to solidify that belief and they'll reward you by sticking around.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** If you hire an exceptional PT, (the ones whose schedules are in high demamd) and you really want them to stick around, offer a path to part ownership of the practice.  At some point, they themselves will want to become uncaged.  This is how a lot of Attorney and Medical practices operate.

> **Response 2:** No. I donâ€™t hire anyone that crazy.

> **Response 2:** the safe approach is to handle performance issues in writing and follow a consistent process so it doesnâ€™t look retaliatory or arbitrary. Hereâ€™s what that normally looks like:
 1. Document clearly â€“ each time something happens, note the date, what occurred, and what policy or expectation wasnâ€™t met. Stick to facts: actions, deadlines missed, or behaviors observed.
 2. Meet and warn â€“ after one or two incidents, have a conversation and summarize it in writing (â€œverbal warning issued on X dateâ€).
 3. Written warning â€“ if it happens again, issue a formal notice describing the problem, the expected correction, and the possible consequences of continued issues. Have the employee sign acknowledgment (not agreement).
 4. Final warning / performance plan â€“ outline a short period to improve (usually 30 days) with measurable goals.
 5. Termination â€“ if thereâ€™s no improvement after documented warnings, you can end employment. Keep all documentation and communicate the decision succinctly and respectfully.

Be sure youâ€™re following:
 â€¢ State and federal labor laws (e.g., anti-discrimination and retaliation protections).
 â€¢ Your own written policiesâ€”consistency is key to legal defensibility.
 â€¢ HR or legal counsel advice if you have it, especially before final termination.

I occasionally lose $ on the PT visits but make it up on the margin of a PTA visit vs pay rate

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I have a wireless plan for my ipad.
I have t-mobile. I've been very happy with it but it's also very different in different areas as far as coverage.

You have to make sure you have an iPad that is cellular capable. Otherwise a mifi device will work. Each carrier has them

I did not find using my phone as a  hotspot to be very reliable the other thing is when you use your phone as a  hotspot at some point it slows your speed. So if you normally get 4G or 5G or hotspot is often 1G less it depends on your carrier and plan. Plus it uses your battery a lot faster

I also found that when I would walk with my patients outside and I had my phone with me it would disconnect from the hotspot and I had to redo it and it was super annoying and I didn't want to have to think about it.
Documentation is hard enough getting it done while you're with the patient so I didn't want anything to make it harder.

> **Response 2:** I just checked into this myself last week. I have an iPad I intend to use for my documentation, but it is a Wi-Fi only device. I checked with my carrier and can add unlimited hotspot to my personal cell plan for $20 per month. This is probably the route Iâ€™m going to take. ï¿¼

**Original Post:**

Goal:  Utilize running as part of my training plan for Grand Canyon Rim-Rim-Rim (4 days with daypack) in June 2024.

â€” I use the Toe Pro and Mobo board inconsistently to work medial/lateral stability.  *Lateral and rotational stability likely needs more attention.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Iâ€™m hypermobile and I run! I have found success with isometrics, particularly hips/glutes. Running with a metronome can help with over-stridingâ€”when youâ€™re floppy itâ€™s easy to over-stride, and this can place more load on the distal musculature on impact. A metronome can help you maintain a cadence and keep some co-contraction of agonists/antagonists (particularly the hips) to keep a more stable proximal base. I use a cadence of somewhere between 160-180 bpm, there are playlists on Spotify that particularly cater to these bpmâ€™s. Hope this helps!

> **Response 2:** I donâ€™t have any advice about running, but I did a hiking R2R a few years ago in September when I was 45 (2 nights at Phantom Ranch so only carried a day pack.)  My 2 cents- the time I put in going up and down the stadium stairs at my local high school wearing my loaded pack that summer was the most beneficial training I did. If you havenâ€™t joined them already, there are R2R and R2R2R fb groups that offer lots of great advice for first-timers. Good luck with your training and enjoy the canyon- there are definitely moments when you need to â€œembrace the suckâ€ but it is an amazing experience ðŸ˜Š

### Discussion 108: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2022-07-24 23:03:09 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 0 reactions, 24 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1017575742346991/

**Original Post:**
When you hire an assistant as a mobile therapist are you doing 1099 or w2?

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Iâ€™m a PT & recently hired a PTA and I was advised (due to my mentorâ€™s lawyerâ€™s advice) that an assistant cannot be 1099 due to them needing supervision of a therapist.  So they cannot function independently as a 1099, only employee.

> **Response 2:** I would be extremely careful about hiring as a 1099. There are both IRS and state laws regarding this and many states are becoming much more vigilant about auditing small businesses for this. I have been through an audit it is very difficulty to prove that they fit the 1099 IC route in most situations for an assistant. Please get very good legal advice on this and be prepared to face an audit on it. The penalties can be significant.

Anyone in a cash practice offers massage or MFR sessions in their clinical practice as an additional revenue stream?

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I am an OT & John F Barnes Myofascial Release (JFB MFR) is my specialty. This is quite different from other forms of MFR. Lots of people specifically seek this modality especially when traditional therapy has not been successful for them. The legality of having someone working on staff will depend on the state. I operate under my OT license in a direct access state. If you're looking for providers doing JFB MFR check out MFR Insight

> **Response 2:** I have a massage therapist in my clinic - I provide her the space - she maintains her license and insurance and pays me 20% per client.  She does her own scheduling and handles her clients payments - so it is a win/win for me.  I have referred several patients to her and vice versa!

### Discussion 117: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2024-09-08 18:13:46 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 4 reactions, 21 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1548765275894699/

**Original Post:**
I am finally creating an LLC in order to treat 2-3 patients a week. Yay! But I have so many questions. I am in Chattanooga, TN and will be treating in a dance studio. Is this the correct order of operations?
1.Get EIN
2.Form LLC
3.Register business with state 
4.File for business license in county 
5.Get liabilty insurance
6.Treat patients

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** If they are treating in a dance studio, it's unlikely they will be seeing Medicare, so that piece might be a moot point. A few things I would add to the list, create a business bank account and get a business only debit card to make taxes much easier,  determine EMR system, create/personalize paperwork for clients - consents, patient policies, intake forms, payment forms, etc. (and remember even if you are cash only, technically you will need a Good Faith Estimate form), and create a policy manual (even if it's just you!) I have 3 studio based clinics and now we have 15 therapists total, so we definitely have to have a policy and procedure manual, but even for my own personal clinic that is just me, I have a document that lists out all my policies -- like cancellation policy for patients, termination policy for patients that aren't a good fit, when I'll do my inventory, how I'll disburse my payments to myself etc. It's one page for my practice, but its helpful to keep me on track! Good luck!

> **Response 2:** Fellow Chattanooga provider! Get after it!!!

### Discussion 123: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-04-30 18:19:20 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 4 reactions, 20 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1730314914406400/

**Original Post:**
For my mobile providers: do you find yourself constantly messing with your schedule to try and keep drives close together as possible, then you DC someone and get someone new who now lived 20 mins the other way and youâ€™re shuffling things all over (and also feel bad for switching current patientâ€™s times)

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Definitely some schedule management. I have 2 different zones, one area M/W, then second area Tues/Thursday that are reasonably close to each other. I do my best to predict, but occasionally ask a patient to slide up or down to avoid zig zagging around town...but I always look a week ahead to prep for that. There are patients that have standing times too. Most are reasonable! I've found I'm able to route decently to be timely, but I do call if I'm more than 5 minutes off.

> **Response 2:** I group and schedule my patients by geographic location. I will even explain this to them during the scheduling process so they understand and none of them have complained at all about it. 

If you think about when you go to the doctor, you just have to take whatever is available. If a patient really wants the service it's not going to make or break you unless of course you only have  an 8:00 a.m. or a 5:00 p.m. or something like that. 

Even with the best laid intentions I have had patients who are 5 minutes away from each other and one has a last-minute doctor appointment and I can't group them together which is frustrating. But it definitely gets easier when you set your boundaries!   

And to make things easier I actually do my schedule only one week at a time. That way I don't waste time moving things around.  Pretty much at the end of their last visit of the week I then go over the schedule for the following week and I put them on. I try to keep their times pretty consistent, just to make scheduling easier.  And I don't allow them to schedule, since I need full control of the calendar based on the geography. ðŸ˜

I actually have two patients right now who live in a neighborhood 30-35 minutes away. That is very far for me but they are both cash pay patients. But I made it very clear to them that because of the distance I have to see both of them on the same day. And they both are fine with it!

### Discussion 129: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2023-08-18 14:00:01 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 26 reactions, 8 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1300710700700159/

**Original Post:**
There are two ditches on both sides of the road to avoid when growing your business:

Left ditch - "I can figure it out on my own." That is fueled by pride/ego and can get us in trouble. It's always healthiest to stay open to learning at all times. 

Right ditch - Over-consuming all information that you can get your hands on. Many people read books and absorb information that isn't helpful in the stage of business they are in, and steers them away from implementation of the right things. 

The heart of this post comes from hearing many people tell me that they have pre-ordered Alex Hormozi's $100M Leads. Every book he puts out is fantastic, no doubt...BUT here is the question I ask each time: Is that what you NEED to be reading to get you to your next level of growth?

If not, be disciplined enough to pick up the RIGHT book.
So, why is this important?

Because I've literally seen practice owners who REALLY just need to hire another PT, pick up a book like that and get side tracked for MONTHS because they are trying to implement the wrong thing.

That book at the RIGHT time for the RIGHT business, Im sure will be exceptional, but really the PT in the example above just needs to focus on hiring, and learning how to do so properly.

Stay on the road at all costs! Don't get distracted and veer yourself off the road only to realize months later how far you have gone off the road. 

You can do this! This is just my reminder to stay focused and avoid the two ditches.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Comparison is how Satan works in businessâ€¦especially for believers. He knows we naturally have desires to have more or do more. When we think we need more or something different comparison starts to run our business and gets us off track

> **Response 2:** Great reminder!!!ðŸ’ªðŸ¼ðŸ¥°

---

### Discussion 135: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2024-04-03 15:31:39 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 5 reactions, 18 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1443593716411856/

**Original Post:**
I own an in home personal training business for seniors in which I provide therapy inspired exercises (private pay). Iâ€™m ready to hire and need any help/advice I can get on hiring a 1099 employee. Iâ€™ve gathered that they need to fill out an agreement, a non compete, and a w9 form. Anything else? Also, should I write up the agreement or do I need a lawyer to do so? Any other other advice is welcome!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Before you move ahead, please understand that a '1099' is a form you issue to any contractor for whom you paid more than $600/year so they can report it on their taxes. (This law is if you're in the USA)

If you're looking for an employee, it's not the same as a '1099'.

By the sounds of what you're looking to do, you probably cannot have independent contractors because the workers will be an integral part of your business.

Here's a blog post that might help understand about the difference between ICs and employees. 

(Ask me how I know!)ðŸ¤¦â€â™€ï¸

https://www.irenediamond.com/are-you-an-really-ic-or-employee

> **Response 2:** As a current 1099 employee, I wouldnâ€™t sign anything with a non compete. My feeling as an independent contractor is I should be able to work for whoever, whenever I want. If you want me to sign a non compete than make me a W2 employee so I donâ€™t get killed in taxes and give me benefits.

**Original Post:**
I'm doing some research on potentially hiring my first PT here in California. It seems like according to CA law, PTs can't be classified as independent contractors. Is this correct? **Have any practice owners in CA hired therapists as independent contractors?** I wanted to hire independent contractors and have them function as PRNs, i.e. setting their own hours and choosing who they want to see. But I need to make sure it's legally sound to bring them on as 1099s instead of W2s.

(The law I'm referring to is AB5 and became effective in January 2020)

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Cannot 1099 in CA under most circumstances.  

Can if itâ€™s something you do not usually or customarily offer. 
But go W9 itâ€™s essentially the same thing.  So bring on a PT that has incorporated themselves and youâ€™re good.   They assume their own liability and risk and insurance etc.  but at that point you become a staffing agency so to speak.

> **Response 2:** I did a lot of research on this too before I hired my first PT in CA, and everything I found pointed to making them a W2 employee. Hope this helps!

### Discussion 155: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-04-14 10:36:35 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 11 reactions, 13 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1717089515728940/

**Original Post:**
I offer personal training as well as physical therapy for my
business. Should I document my personal training sessions?

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** While not legally required to, I document a visit happened, and 2-3 sentences of what happened. 

Usually any major data points I have invented for the client: 30 min walking distance, weight vest laps around living environment, time to do complete 50 sit to stands, etc 

Main reason I do this is to be a better trainer and remember benchmarks as well as tax purposes to deduct driven miles for each session.

> **Response 2:** When I did personal training, I had a simple chart with all the exercises down the side and dates across the top. In each column, I recorded weight, #reps, time under load. ï¿¼ at the very bottom of the column, you could write any significant notes (like where you focused on technique, tolerance, etc.).  This way you have a record and are tracking progress easily. ï¿¼

### Discussion 164: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-07-11 17:01:28 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 6 reactions, 15 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1787430205361537/

**Original Post:**
How do you guys hire/find new PT's? I live in a smaller town, close to a huge city, about an hour away. But If I could, I could hire 4-5 more PT's based on how busy we are. But It is so hard to find anyone right now. I've done job fairs but that's more long term Investing In hiring someone.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Do you take students?  That might be a nice way to train and recruit future therapists get awareness for your practice.

> **Response 2:** When recruiting therapists, no matter where, active recruiting is a must. 

So not just posting a job and hoping/waiting for applicants. Getting a licensure list from your state which usually will include emails (and hopefully phone numbers), emailing, texting, calling to those is the zip codes close to you. 

Posting on social media/linkedIn. 

Get in touch with the local PT schools in your area and try and connect with those last year PT students. 

Differentiating your job when you post it. Highlight the reasons someone would want to work for you. Also donâ€™t list every duty/the entire job description in the post. Itâ€™s not necessary and no one reads it. 

Itâ€™s so important to get back to applicants the same day and set up an interview asap. Then make a decision quickly.

---

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** We use hello note. Very inexpensive and customer service is on top of it with any issues. Not a lot of problems and very user friendly. Also has a billing platform built in.

> **Response 2:** We switched from WebPT to Prompt. WebPT became too glitchy with lost documentation in the middle of a note, at one point frequent outages which may now be fixed. 
We are with Prompt now, I wish I would have looked at more but the ease of documentation was unmatched. It is more expensive, with hidden â€œadd onâ€ purchases including an automatic fax button at the end of notes. But at the end of the day, the transition was smooth. Very user friendly. And therapists are happy with the features. The billing system is very user friendly. 
May consider switching to something cheaper in the future.

### Discussion 175: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2024-08-21 17:02:24 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 30 reactions, 2 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1536065393831354/

**Original Post:**
Just some PSAs for y'all.

- Stay active in your local groups. Especially ones where people are frequently connecting with each other ("who do you use for hair/nails/doctor/dentist/PT/gym/personal training").

- Connect with people who are doing things like what you do. They will advocate for you! AND now you know people to refer out to when you're not the right fit.

- Plan WAYYYYY in advance for who to hire and how to hire. I just got 6 new evals because of one connection, and it's going to swamp my schedule. And I am not prepared to hire -- learn from my mistake. ðŸ« 

Keep on truckin', y'all.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Happy to help out:)

> **Response 2:** â¤ï¸

My husband isnâ€™t in healthcare and gets 3wk 100% paid leave.. his company breaks it down that both parents get 3wk for â€œfamily bondingâ€ and this can be used for any situation - adoption, birth, etc. The birthing person gets an additional 9wk paid leave for â€œphysical recoveryâ€, so 12 wk total for them. 

Paid leave is the right thing to do for both parents, and (sadly) offering this would set you apart from the rest of the healthcare field. I know youâ€™re probably a small company, and it really should be the big orgs that are doing this, but if you can, please offer it!

> **Response 2:** I think itâ€™s hard for any employer to do this, but my personal opinion is that at least partially covering paid parental leave is the right thing to do and youâ€™ll have a more loyal staff because of it. Family first.

Thanks guys!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Some home health companies will hire your LLC as a staffing company. So if you have PTAs who you can hire under your LLC as 1099s you can offer the agency PT staffing from eval to DC by your staffing company.  Then you can make a little bit off each visit done by your PTAs. In Florida all you need is to get a Health Care Services Pool license. $600 every two years.

I use square for payments, Setmore for appt scheduling, mailer lite for email marketing, google docs for intake, and the notes app for client notes.  I save notes to my google drive

### Discussion 199: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2023-07-07 16:57:21 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 4 reactions, 13 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1276819596422603/

**Original Post:**
Hello! We are hiring our first employee for admin work (answering calls, scheduling, verifying insurnace, etc). 

Looking if anyone has any tips and tricks for making it a smooth process or anything you used to help as this will be a remote position. 

I will still be taking over some of the admin duties part of the day and then our employee we are hiring will be working the later half of each day.

Not exactly sure what Iâ€™m looking for, but just want to see how others handle this as Iâ€™m putting together some training resources and envisioning how everything will work between sharing duties split between the hours of the day. 

TIA! â˜ºï¸

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Hi! I manage our admin Team. If this will be remote position, you'll need to set the tone for productivity and priorities from day 1. I also recommend them coming in a day or couple of shifts during the week if possible.

The greatest impact that one can have is keeping your schedule full.. time is of the essence. I call it the window of opportunity. If a patient no shows, cancels, or says they'll have to call back to schedule. They go on a call list.. calls need to be made the next day, then the very next day. If we wait until a week after their missed appointment, then the likelihood of them getting back on the schedule drops by 70%.

Referrals called same day, then the next day. Same window of opportunity applies.

These call back and referral lists should be on a spreadsheet shared via secured server so that you can see real time updates. Calls should be made at the best times. Before 9AM and after 5PM. Why? That is when people answer because that is when they are off from work.

Authorizations should be kept on a log as well with approval/denial status and visits/date range approved.

Schedule a weeks worth of appointments at a time.

Send eval/progress note updates to referring providers weekly to keep them informed and your business front and center (out of sight out of mind).

Give little bonuses/incentives for clinic growth. "If we increase by __% of visits, or if we average ___ visits for the month, then we'll give___" or "If you schedule __% of referrals that came in you get___"

Lastly, invest in remote work tools:

Ring Central so they can send and recieve faxes via email.

VOIP phone service to make and take calls from a number linked to your business. Look for an option that will provide call logs and volume so you can see how much or how little they have on their plate.

I always look for people with previous Medical office experience, sales is a plus. Must have excel, outlook, MS office experience.

Congratulations on your growth! ðŸ™Œ

> **Response 2:** Hey Amanda congrats on the growth. We employ a ton of admins for practices across the country. 

Big keys. Make sure you define success. What metrics/KPIs drive this position and how will you measure success. 

Make sure you have all of your log ins and scripts/SOPs in one location so that it is very easy for the admin to access. 

I find that measuring hours can be very difficult for a virtual admin so often times paying then a flat rate for a set of hours or tasks often work at the best.

---

> **Response 1:** I have been 1099 for the past 4 years- as the person hiring 1099, you can not provide anything perceived as a benefit. The company I contract with does organize CEU courses under another consulting company umbrella for us, but we must pay a reasonable amount for it. Ie 16 hours cost us 175 dollars this year. 1099 laws vary in different states but they largely all say that you cannot dictate a minimum number of hours nor directly supervise how they provide the work. If you want control I suggest a PRN employee.

> **Response 2:** Discuss cancellation, no shows and rescheduled appts

### Discussion 237: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2023-01-09 15:24:04 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 3 reactions, 12 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1155122451925652/

**Original Post:**
Hello everyone! Happy new year.

I wanted to get advice on how to manage being busy. I have gotten very very busy, to the point where I have patients on a waitlist. I hate this because I hate patients not being able to get in. Subconsciously I just feel bad and that people will talk bad about how they canâ€™t get in.

But what I really need advice for is:

1. how I can have my secretary/front office person manage better with so much going on and with scheduling. And how to properly explain to patients that we will get them in as soon as we can. Are there any iMac applications or softwares we can buy where we can create a daily checklist to follow so we donâ€™t miss anything?

2. As far as when talking to the patients, because we have some patients who canâ€™t get the times that they want or have to come very early or very late, any advice on how to manage this?

3. We get a lot of referrals via primary cares and word of mouth, how do we handle it now that we are so busy? I cannot fathom the idea of telling physicians to stop sending patients as I donâ€™t want to hurt the relationships we have with them.

4. I know the big obvious answer is to hire someone, and Iâ€™ve been looking (definitely not hard enough) but any advice on this too? I donâ€™t live in a super popular big city so itâ€™s definitely not going to be a first choice for a lot of people. But I looked hard last summer to hire someone and had no luck at all.

Thanks everyone and look forward to hearing your advice. Thanks!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Hire and work on the systems up front and with the hire.  So they keep the level that you patients have come to expect.  Checklist, for what. What is the goal of making sure nothing is missed.  What might your frond office miss.  Automate that process where you can

> **Response 2:** Always easy to say hire, not as easily done, but get the process started. What a phenomenal  problem to have!! Congratulations!! Be proud! One way to handle this is to consider your perfect/ideal patient  and start prioritizing  that way. As therapist we always want to help everyone, however, that's not possible. This is a great time for you to streamline and determine what you really want your business to become. You have options now without a doubt. If there is a population that lights your fire as a practitioner go that direction or, even if it is challenging for therapist to change their perspective this way, go towards an area of practice which increases your profitability. Is that insurance, or a population who would prefer to pay per service instead of insurance, or pay for additional alternative/ non-insurance reimbursed treatments? You are in high demand and you shouldn't feel bad about that, not for one second! Make sure your front desk handles it with Grace and with empathy but also not with shame. If you give the perspective that you are doing something wrong by not getting everyone in the door right away, the takeaway will be a negative. Flip it so that the wait list is a positive and one that creates further desire for the patient to want to wait

---

### Discussion 238: [HIGH ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2022-06-24 23:25:20 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 15 reactions, 6 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/996021604502405/

**Original Post:**
Now that you are uncaged, how are you all making your business a place where itâ€™s not like these corporate corporations? How do you show appreciation for your employees? How are your processes and procedure tailored to your employees having a good work/life balance? 
Asking for myself and my company. 

Thanks!!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** First of all, I am grateful daily for every single person that works WITH me (I don't say FOR me). I once heard, "it is a virtual miracle that your employees show up to work. They don't have to". So I make sure to say "thanks" a LOT.
#2 I ASK them if they can take patients. I don't do their scheduling. I treat them like the intelligent, competent, adults they are. No one likes to be micromanaged.
#3 I don't believe in productivity. In this field, it is absolutely unwarranted and ruining healthcare. 
#4 I ask how I can be of service to them. It is my belief that as admin, my job is supporting the staff in the field. (I own a home health staffing company). It's not easy to drive from patient to patient, call doctors, communicate with the care team. If I can make their day easier by doing a menial task, I do it!
(I should add that everyone who works with me is an independent contractor and has complete choice over their schedule. As a 1099, I'm able to offer them more freedom)

> **Response 2:** Ooooh this is such a great question ðŸ‘ðŸ¼ 
Iâ€™m a solopreneur, but Iâ€™m excited to hear everyoneâ€™s answers! 

I take hikes, work outside, say no to businesses that donâ€™t align, and strive to eventually be â€œa job maker, not a job takerâ€

When did you know you were able to switch from offering a 1099 position to an hourly W-2 or salaried position? Iâ€™m scheduling an appt with my accountant but wanted to hear from people in practices. I have a 1099 clinician that is at about 20 direct contact hours. SLP practice. Thanks.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Agreeing with what everyone said about misclassification.  1099 = you do not dictate their schedule, you do not provide them with any tools or equipment, you do not mandate a dress code, etc.  In other words, they provide you a service.  Think of it as hiring the repairman.  You hire him to do "x" job but he comes when he can, brings his own tools and wears what he wants.  Anything else is a W2.  W2= if you dictate their work hours or schedule, you provide them with equipment and you tell them to wear scrubs.  *hope that helps

> **Response 2:** From talking to a lawyer here in CO many people are misclassified as â€œ1099â€ that really are W2 employees. Have you looked at the requirements for classification for both categories? Or consulted with an attorney?

---

**Original Post:**
What do you all have for brick and mortar building security system and entrance door? However I also donâ€™t want someone strange walking in to the building? It is an ok neighborhood but there are crimes everywhere? What do you all do?

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I have a similar set up.  I have a security camera in the waiting room that records when thereâ€™s movement and I can review recorded videos and live streaming on an app on my phone. 

I have chimes that sounds when the front door opens. 

I can lock the door between the waiting room and the rest of my office.

A few years ago I had some problems with some really creepy guy patients so I have a few other safety measures too:

Apple Watch because of the press and hold security feature  

Waistband toggle that makes an ear piercing sound if removed from the waistband

And hornet spray (one of my patients thatâ€™s a police officer recommended this). It shoots a stream 20-30 feet and doesnâ€™t create a cloud that could also affect you.  He said to aim for the eyes.  I have one in my rollie computer desk and a few others in various places around the office.

> **Response 2:** I wonder if you could use something like Level, depending on the type of door? You could have a standard key lock for full opening and closing and then use a temporary pass for your patients if they show up a few minutes early and want to use the secondary Level lock.

### Discussion 255: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2023-09-13 15:34:57 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 5 reactions, 10 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1316825732421989/

**Original Post:**
Hi Everyone,

I'm in need of a pep talk or any advice. 
We've just surpassed 1 year of business and have been on track with our goals. 
However, recently, we've had SO MANY cancellations. It's starting to wear me down. Both myself and my other therapist on staff are dealing with this and it's making me feel like I'm doing something wrong or people don't think we are worth It. Since August we've had at least a few a week (minimum) or shuffling around the schedule. I know I shouldn't focus on that because we've also had so many great wins but sometimes it's hard and I want to minimize this going forward. As a side we are all cash pay. 
Thanks for your help!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** First off, that can be completely normal this time of the year. You are doing great! If you are on track with your goals, then just focus on the wins and less on the losses. 

If the cancellations become a consistent problem, then go back and focus on communication and how the plan of care is communicated during the evaluation and during each treatment to the clients. That can usually clear up cancellation problems.

> **Response 2:** So the question is what are you doing about it?
...
Once you acknowledge the problem the next step is developing a system to resolve it and prevent it. 
...
There are lots of ways to fix this problem. 
...
Some therapists will impose strict cancel fees, others will secure payment in advance. 
...
Personally I find that this is a signal that my marketing is targeting the wrong patients. When I stopped treating low back pain referrals and focused on post op TKR referrals my cancel/no show rate dropped to near zero. 
...
It is normal to feel frustrated, but that is when you put on your business owner hat and realize you can control the situation and make a change.

---

### Discussion 263: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2022-05-20 19:31:29 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 5 reactions, 10 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/971357466968819/

**Original Post:**
Question: how does one hire someone?  Legal stuff, contracts, payroll, benefits, etc.  Explain this to me like Iâ€™m a 5 year old.  ðŸ˜…

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** That depends greatly if you want a 1099 or W2 :)

> **Response 2:** 1. Hire employment attorney 
2. Determine contract type

1099 no extra bells and whistles but the attorney is necessary to make sure you are compliant with the law. Most contractors should actually be W2 employeesâ€¦.you can, and likely will, get audits from the IRS with 1099 contractors.

The following is for W2
3. Benefits are through a benefits broker. You can find them online or at networking events
4. Contact CPA and bookkeeper to determine best payroll system. 
5. Create onboarding strategy, policies and procedures, handbook.
6. File for state unemployment insurance and update LLC 
7. Purchase business liability and umbrella policy.
8. Get quotes for adding therapist to malpractice.
9. Get someone to agree to salary 
10. Sign contract
11. Add them to policies
12. Add them to any insurance contracts
13. W4 and I9 process
14. Get ready to pay taxes

### Discussion 265: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-07-23 20:32:02 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 2 reactions, 11 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1797377897700101/

**Original Post:**
I recently rented a space in a holistic cash based practice. I am the only PT amongst NPS, chiros, massage therapist , sound therapist, yoga etc. I have been asked to participate in their marketing event and do short paid sessions of cupping or MFR

Can I do hands on sessions without a proper eval, should I have the clients fill out consent forms?

If not what other services/ consults can I offer?

I don't want to miss the opportunity to introduce myself to prospective clients. I am in NC..

Any ideas?

TIA

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** How is it set up? Open house type deal, or are participants flowing from one section to another on a schedule of sorts? Free flowing open house events, I do better with postural screenings and being able to interact in small groups because splitting off one person to set up cupping can get awkward. If it is a round robin- groups come and spend 15 minutes with each provider, or individuals sign up for 10 minute â€œtasterâ€ sessions, then I would prepare short presentations for groups or do the hands on (consent forms always!) if they are coming over individually. Truly, being able to ask questions and respond to the person/group in front of you is pretty impactful without a hands on demo- I usually gain clients from doing this in a social atmosphere. Good luck!

> **Response 2:** Iâ€™m no lawyer, but Iâ€™d def get a signed consent form and have them fill out a health questionnaire to CYA and screen them w a quick eval - whatever that looks like for you. Document as well, even if you have some forms on hand printed out for them and a quick way for you to document what you assessed and what you did. 

Make sure your liability insurance covers you out of the office if this is offsite. 

Im assuming NC is a direct access state?

**Original Post:**
For those of you that do not work with insurances and provide cash based services such as dry needling, taping, manipulation techniques, and other holistic health and wellness/pain management services, what do you typically label your invoices for and what type of documentation are you using for both liability protection and reference points (whether thatâ€™s for your patients personal information or for a repeat customer to track modalities and treatments utilized)? **Original Post:**
For mobile practice, what's the best EMR? What are the downsides and upsides? Thanks.

**Community Responses:**

### Discussion 277: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2024-11-01 18:04:21 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 2 reactions, 11 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1590432788394614/

**Original Post:**
I'm hiring my first contract employee. I'm a single member LLc but for tax purposes, and S corp.  What things do I need to consider in doing this? I have an employee contract, way to do payroll.  Do I need to add her to my liability insurance??  But I assume she carries her own too?  She will get a percentage of the visit plus the surcharge for the travel will be hers.  Is she responsible for her own equipment?  She will use my EMR... What else am I missing?  Thank you!!!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Congratulations on hiring your first contractor! Hereâ€™s a rundown of essential considerations:

1. Independent Contractor Classification: Make sure she meets the requirements for a 1099 contractor, not a W-2 employee. This means she should have flexibility in how and when she works, supply some of her own equipment, and take on some business risks (like travel expenses).

2. Insurance: Yes, youâ€™ll want her to carry her own liability insurance. Itâ€™s still a good idea to confirm this with your own insurer, as they might require you to list contractors for full coverage. Having clear documentation of her liability coverage can help protect both of you.

3. Contract Specifics: Make sure your contract covers:

Payment Terms: Outline the percentage per visit, any reimbursement for travel, and payment timelines.

Confidentiality and HIPAA Compliance: Since sheâ€™s using your EMR, include specific language about HIPAA compliance and patient data security.

Non-compete or Non-solicitation Clauses: Decide if you want any limitations around her working with your clients independently.

4. EMR Access and Compliance: Ensure sheâ€™s trained on your EMR and understands your documentation standards. Since sheâ€™s using your system, emphasize that she adheres to the same security measures you do.

5. Equipment: If sheâ€™s responsible for her own equipment, be clear about what is needed to fulfill the job (e.g., laptop, mobile device, therapy tools) and ensure this is in writing. Anything you provide would technically be taxable, so itâ€™s easier for her to provide her own if she can.

6. Payroll and Taxes: If she's a 1099 contractor, you wonâ€™t withhold taxes for her, but make sure to issue her a 1099-NEC at the end of the year for tax purposes. Keep detailed payment records to help her accurately report her income.

7. Workerâ€™s Compensation: While 1099 contractors typically arenâ€™t covered by workerâ€™s comp, itâ€™s worth checking your stateâ€™s requirements, as some have specific regulations for certain industries.

8. Clear Communication: Especially with your first hire, be proactive in setting up regular check-ins to make sure everything is running smoothly. A strong onboarding process will help set clear expectations and keep the working relationship positive.

Starting with these steps will help lay a solid foundation for both of you!

> **Response 2:** I hired two people this year, one W2 and one independent. Their rolls for employment are very different. For W2, I have a number of associated costs (disability, liability, payroll taxes, mileage stipend, health insurance, etc). My independent contractor has none of those associated costs/benefits. She is paid a flat fee for service/per session rate vs my w2 who is hourly. Independent carries her own insurance and pays her own taxes on what she receives. States and fed is VERY specific about differentiating between the two. Carefully do your research and decide what role you want your new hire to have. And be specific.  The contract you have this person sign should state what type of hire they are.

---

"Under the ABC test, a worker is considered an employee and not an independent contractor, unless the hiring entity satisfies all three of the following conditions:
1. The worker is free from the control and direction of the hiring entity in connection with the performance of the work, both under the contract for the performance of the work and in fact;
2.The worker performs work that is outside the usual course of the hiring entityâ€™s business; and
3. The worker is customarily engaged in an independently established trade, occupation, or business of the same nature as that involved in the work performed."

Help please :(

Question in regards to documenting levels of assistance with Medicare . Examples as follows: 1) if a therapist needs to bring w/c behind someone for rest breaks (patient is steady)  when walking with FWW what level of assistance is this labeled as (Min A, CGA/SBA) 2) If a therapist needs to navigate the O2 tank while someone is walking steadily with a FWW, what level of assistance is documented? 3) If a therapist has to navigate a catheter during an activity (stairs, walking, picking up objects) and patient is steady , what level of assistance is given ? > **Response 1:** You can also document SBA walking with maxA for managing O2/catheter etc.

Realistically this patient needs to have a discussion with their pulmonologist to get a portable concentrator since itâ€™s nearly impossible for a person to to use a FWW and O2 tank safely unless itâ€™s hooked or adhered to the FWW.

I have a separate spreadsheet where I track what's been sent and when it comes back. I admit it's a bit of a hassle. I wish Jane had a fax system integrated.

> **Response 2:** I use Srfax with SimplePractice. Make a chart note when I fax POC for signature and also have a spread sheet of 1st/2nd attempts, when receive signed POC, when cert expires, when D/C and color code. I upload pdf of signed POC (naming document with end date of certification of POC) to patient chart and if needed make â€œother apptâ€ on the day cert POC is up as another reminder.

### Discussion 297: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2024-08-15 22:31:01 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 6 reactions, 8 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1532062560898304/

**Original Post:**
I started my cash-based mobile vestibular practice in April and thinking about offering a telehealth option. I donâ€™t have an EMR, I use Google Workspace and just signed up with doxy.me. What do I need to do to set this up? Telehealth patient consent form? Anything else? Thanks in advance!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Telehealth and mobile vestibular PT here!  You have to document that you used audio and visual format using doxy.me for telehealth appointments, and you have to document the individual's address at the time of service (okay to say "refer to address in intake paperwork").  You also have to be licensed in the state where the patient is located at the time of the service.

> **Response 2:** 1) You can use Google Workspace as an EMR. Check out Unsubscribed Healthcare on YouTube. 

2) Our state practice act (KY) had information on what they needed us to have on file. Or maybe it was Medicare... Pretty sure it was our practice act though. It was pretty straightforward, just a couple forms and some things to verbally verify at the front of each telehealth session.

### Discussion 307: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2023-02-28 16:41:33 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 0 reactions, 11 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1192933594811204/

**Original Post:**
Hey everyone! 

When hiring a contract PTA (W2/1099 contractor), what have you been responsive for as the employer and what have you had the independent contractor be responsible regarding:

Lliability insurance
NPI (secondary needed if they work at another facility?)
Workers comp insurance? 
Reimbursing for Mileage (if mobile)

Thanks!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I was under the impression that a PTA could not be an independent contractor as they have to work under your license, so they must be a W2 employee...

> **Response 2:** A contractor must be either/or W2 or 1099. I do not provide anything for the 1099 other than a higher rate. A 1099 is able to write off the cost of liability insurance, equipment, and mileage. A W2 cannot.
I do have workers comp for them only because some of our contracted home health agencies require it for their certifications (CHAPS or JACHO)

### Discussion 315: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-05-22 01:50:51 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 1 reactions, 10 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1746547529449805/

**Original Post:**
How do you set up your scheduling software if you are mobile? It canâ€™t be on the hourâ€¦ðŸ¤·ðŸ½â€â™€ï¸ðŸ¤·ðŸ½â€â™€ï¸

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I schedule myself so I can have control over when I see them. Based on exactly where they live. I try to keep patients closer together so there's no backtracking and it's more efficient. I use Google Calendar and love it.

For my own sanity I schedule one week at a time. When I'm approaching their final visit of the week, I ask if there are any upcoming appointments that I need to know about. Then I go ahead and schedule them for the next week. 

I do this because at least one patient has some conflicting appointment that causes me to have to change their time slightly. And their appointments tend to change or get canceled. 

Generally allow 30 minutes in between visits for any documentation time, if I run late, traffic etc.

> **Response 2:** 1 hour slot, 30 min travel and/or doc time.

You want to make sure you understand their needs so they come to you for answers
