### Discussion 339: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-08-08 15:48:11 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 2 reactions, 9 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1810778836360007/

**Original Post:**
Looking for advice from those that have scaled a solo practice:  I currently have a solo cash based practice in one room   Average 25ish visits a week.  I have the opportunity to rent a larger space with 3 treatment rooms, better visibility and in the same strip mall Im currently in.  I enjoy the freedom I have not dealing with any co-workers.  But  I have concerns over long term viability if I don't expand and would like to build an asset.  I am considering hiring a part time PT (if I can find one) at 15-20 hours/week.  What are the pros and cons and other considerations I need to consider? TIA

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** In my opinion you have to at bare minimum grow to where you have at least 1 person underneath you solely for the reason of being able to take vacation and god forbid you get hurt or sick. The business has to cash flow while youâ€™re out otherwise you just have risk. 

Starting part time is a great idea. I would make sure you have 3-6 months of payroll in the bank and an emergency fund prob 3 months of operating costs. I would also start building credit by establishing LOCs at various banks (do this while times are good because when you need it itâ€™s hard to get). 

Once you have that established a part time hire is a great way to go. Just donâ€™t bite off more than you can chew.

> **Response 2:** Have you thought about hiring a PTA instead? You can do evals and PNs and they do the treatments. See if you can legally bring them on as a contractor.

The biggest benefit to building a team is that you can take off time (sickness, kids soccer game etc.) while the company continues to run and patients still get seen. You can 
 make a lot more money. You can build a company that has value if you ever want or need to sell it.

Cons: a lot of new work, new learning, your no longer just a PT, you have to learn how to hire, train, lead,oversee etc. operations have to be decent, learn a lot of laws, learn payroll, HR etc etc etc.

Itâ€™s not for everyone, and while it is definitely the â€œglamorousâ€ position to be in, I wouldnâ€™t recommend it if you are not fully in it. Sometimes you donâ€™t know if you are built for it until you try it though. For me, I enjoy it but I donâ€™t think I can do it forever.

There is no correct answer, you need to look at what you want to build and decide if you want to take on a new job that you have no experience in. What is the goal? How much do you want to grow? What do you want your life to look like? If you have a family, what are their thoughts with you taking on a new position filled with more frustration and challenges.

If you have any specific questions, Iâ€™d be more than happy to help out.

Ps. I purposely donâ€™t proofread these kind of messages so that it comes out honest and raw, and not sugarcoated in any way.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I'm also in VA. I've used Square and currently use intakeq. For both systems as long as I'm registered with them as a healthcare provider the client can just process the HSA/FSA as they would a normal credit card. 

There's no additional documentation requirements. Sometimes they may need to submit a superbill for proof the funds were used foe medical/health services, but this hasn't been necessary for any of my clients as my business is registered as healthcare with my payment systems.

> **Response 2:** Iâ€™m cash based in VA. I use a payment app (HIPPA compliant) called IvyPay

The family puts CC directly into there for payment. It actually also allows the family to put in HSA or FSA accounts if they prefer to pay from those

> **Response 2:** Since you said that the cancellation fee/policy is in your paperwork and reviewed with the client, then I would 100% charge this. I am also mobile and if someone was to cancel with 8 minutes to go to their appt, I would charge them my full cancellation fee. The only way I wouldn't do this if it was a super extenuating circumstance, i.e. they got into a car accident on the way home from errands. From your example, this client very likely knew they were ill before 11:22am - if they woke up at 9am and felt ill, they should have notified you as early as possible. I get it that some circumstances are different, but they need to respect your time.

### Discussion 379: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2023-08-18 02:23:31 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 2 reactions, 8 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1301448320626397/

**Original Post:**
Looking for advice on publishing a special populations wellness book. I have the bulk of the content done but am stuck on a few aspects:

-how much time/money to invest on formatting and graphics until I figure out if it will be self publishing vs sending manuscripts to publishers (who I assume would give input and have their own team to assist with that). 
-Is Amazon KDP what others of you used or are there better self publishing options if thatâ€™s the recommended route? 
-Do I need to set up an LLC now (or ever) just for publishing? I worry since the book is exercise/wellness despite multiple disclaimers it could be a liability. 

Thanks for any guidance. I feel stuck and really am hoping to get this out.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** We did a session on this at a summit in June.. where are you at in the process. KDP is definitely a great route to start with.

> **Response 2:** I just published my first book last week, went through KDP since I was a newbie at this. Didn't check out other self-publishing options; needed to get it out. I can answer a couple of your questions: 
--I wanted a good quality book, so I invested $$ in editing and cover design/graphics and illustrations. With self-publishing, your deadlines are your own, not dictated by a publisher (pros and cons for that). Find a graphics person who understands and follows copyright laws! Found out that the formatting had to be done by me or my husband as I couldn't give account access to my cover artist. THAT took a long time and energy. On the flip side, I don't have to pay any publishing, printing, or distribution costs with KDP. 
--I published in KDP as an individual author and not through my business. Thought that doing this would allow me to use it as an educator and advocate and not just my PT clinic's product. Hope that makes sense!
--I get it, it is easy to get stuck at this phase. Trust me that this Uncaged group is great at helping you get unstuck! Right Sharon Gaffney-Wisnewski Josh Payne?? ðŸ™‚

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Following because I have a similar issue. My plan was to institute a new policy effective Jan 1 - cancellation/no show policy and a fee for nonpayment of invoices after a certain time period, as Iâ€™m also having an issue with that, albeit a much smaller problem than the cancelations.

> **Response 2:** I give out a form that the clients sign with initial paperwork stating that my cancelation policy is a $100 fee for less that 24 hours notice. The first time a client cancels without rescheduling I remind them that they sign this form in the initial paperwork and tell them that this time I will not charge them but any future cancellations will be charged. I also make them understand that by them canceling last
Minute they are preventing another client from receiving care. People usually think that is reasonable and will respect your time going forward. If you have a repeat offender that never keeps appointments I would just tell them that you can not keep them on your schedule but we happy to try to accommodate same day visit if they call and you have availability. For what itâ€™s worth Iâ€™m cash pay except for Medicare

### Discussion 411: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2023-07-24 18:30:29 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 0 reactions, 8 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1287060538731842/

**Original Post:**
Hello!

So we have a new PT starting in august. Really just waiting for her license to come in and she can start instantly. So Iâ€™m just guessing it hopefully comes in mid august. So maybe august 14 or august 21.

So the week of the 14th I have 7 new evalâ€™s scheduled. Iâ€™m really hoping to be able to give these new evals to our new PT. So I wanted to re schedule them to the following week where the new PT will have her license in and she can start with them.

But i dont know how to call the patients who are already scheduled, who will have been waiting for almost 3-4 weeks to be seen that I want to move them back another week?

Because if they stay on my schedule it will be very hard to get them scheduled for follow up appointments.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** personally, if these patients waited that long, they want to see you!  To schedule them with someone isn't fair; but you may also lose patients- because why wait longer if they can't see you to begin with?
 Maybe what you can do, especially if the new clinican is a new grad is have them come "shadow" the day you're loaded with evals. 
This way patients can also see who else is in the clinic.

We had similar situations happen at a few clinics where I worked. Some patients only wanted to see one clinician because of past word of mouth and that's okay. 
However, you can use this time to let patients know, we have someone new coming in, to help with my caseload...talk that therapist up! It may work to your advantage vs rescheduling patients to a later week.

> **Response 2:** You do the evals then hand off.  Have the new therapist observe and type up the eval if you are overwhelmed.   Itâ€™s much more important to get those patients in the door to start.   If patients have to wait 4-5 weeks for PT they are much more likely to go elsewhere or no show.   ðŸ¤·â€â™€ï¸

**Date:** 2023-12-23 04:25:17 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 1 reactions, 7 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1378411179596777/

**Original Post:**
For those of you that use Google Workspace for forms... How do you have patients complete these? Bring your laptop and have them do it online or send forms ahead of time? Print and upload later?  Thanks in advance!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I have Google forms that I send out to patients. The data they enter is stored in a spreadsheet, populates a template I can save as a PDF, and fills out half the history section of my eval note.

> **Response 2:** I send the forms ahead of time and have them fill it all out online. If they have trouble filling it out online, I show up early and fill it out for them on my own device.

I found that Google Forms were not very print friendly, but were great if I just let Google Workspace do its thing lol.

### Discussion 435: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2023-03-02 21:38:50 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 3 reactions, 6 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1194464111324819/

**Original Post:**
Hey everyone! Looking to get feedback on your follow up protocols when someone has expressed interest in booking but then doesn't get back to you. Also, how and how often you follow up after the initial visit when they don't want to book another appointment right then and there, but say they will go on the website to book. Thanks!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I always follow the initial evaluation with a detailed email telling them what we discussed and their exercises. At the end of the email, I remind them I typically see patients less often than a traditional therapist and ask them to reach out with their needs. After a week (regardless if they scheduled another appointment) I do a quick follow up email to make sure exercises are going well. After that, I tend to let them go as they probably wouldnâ€™t be a good fit for me. They tend to schedule another appointment between those 2 emails thoughðŸ˜Š Hope this helps!

> **Response 2:** Bumping because I need help, please!

### Discussion 439: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-11-18 18:22:16 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 1 reactions, 7 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1901788047259085/

**Original Post:**
1099 vs W2

I have a solo OT mobile practice and am wanting to bring on a COTA for some extra help. Currently it would be between 2-5 visits per week. They would have complete autonomy with scheduling and interventions completed during the visits. Iâ€™m wondering if I could pay someone higher rates and 1099 them or if W2 would be better for them? Thank you for any input - still trying to figure out the business side of all of this ðŸ˜…

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** The very nature of a OTA position requires W-2 given you are in a supervisory capacity as the OT and they cannot function autonomously.

> **Response 2:** W2 is the correct, legal way to go with this. There is a podcast that Nicole Cozean and her husband did on the difference between 1099 versus W2 but ultimately if they provider has a set schedule, they are W2.

### Discussion 443: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2024-01-11 17:23:44 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team

**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1390525071718721/

**Original Post:**
If I hire a PTA for prn work, and they make their own schedule, etc, can they ever be considered a 1099? Or would they have to be a W2 as they require supervision from a PT?

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I have PTAs as 1099. They make their own schedule and have the ability to decline patients. The supervision from a PT portion is a licensure requirement but doesn't mean you are telling the PTA exactly what to do and when.

> **Response 2:** I think it will really depend on how you set it up and possibly your state. I have a couple friends who were audited here and Utah and got fines. Could be an Utah thing. Could be how they set it up. I have all my PTAs as W2 just to avoid that problem.

### Discussion 448: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-11-24 00:43:07 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 0 reactions, 7 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1906128450158378/

**Original Post:**
Ive never had anyone ask to share their pt info with anyone else, so i dont have a form yet for this- but someone called asking about pt for her son, i assumed under 18- no- in his 20s. I said he has to call to schedule himself and bring his forms in person etc. i assume i need a form in case he wants to consent to her receiving any info (if he asks, but sounds like she will be paying)- anyone have one they can share for this scenario? Thanks

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I have had parents schedule and pay for their young adult children. Because of HIPAA the young adult must give consent for the parent to have access to their medical records if they choose to do so. I've also had adult children schedule and pay for their parents. Same rules apply. They pay and understand that unless the patient gives written consent for them to have access to any of their medical history them I cannot release it. The financial agreement indicates that the party paying is aware that their card will be charged, but ultimately the responsibility falls in the patient.

> **Response 2:** So i do with dd ddis a i just have form they full out.

> **Response 1:** Insurance should cover the imaging if it is medically necessary.

> **Response 2:** I send them to PCP with a note from me and sharing about "possibly" needing further imaging as I suspect xxx. Or if they see a Chiropractor, I ask them to call their chiro and ask for a referral for imaging, again sending them with a note or giving them the wording for that conversation.

### Discussion 497: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-07-17 13:39:56 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools

**Original Post:**
I have a question regarding releasing documentation to patients with evident mental health issues... I understand that it's within their rights to request that, but how should I do it?

One of my patients decided to discharge herself because she claimed that she "felt worse and less self-worthy" every time she came to our clinic. She made a lot of false accusations and her reasoning was inconsistent, invalid and irrelevant. (She claimed that my boss was attacking her personally while my boss made comments on past employees and events that were completely unrelated to her. My boss never even worked with her once. And I got accused for not defending her and lack of compassion when I tried to clarify what my boss's words to resolve the misunderstanding.)

I'm not trying to diagnose her, but this appeared to be like persecutory delusion to me. She was a long-term patient, and over time I also learned about her several past traumas (with suicidal ideations at some point before seeing me) and attempts to seek counseling.

She told me not to document any part of the conversations. But I did and stated that "psychosocial disorders are suspected, and mental health interventions should be prioritized."

Now as she is requesting her notes, I'm not sure if we should just give her directly. I am really worried that her mental condition would deteriorate from reading my notes. To abide by my ethics, if I foresee an action that would do harm to my patient, I should avoid it, right? But can I "not" give her the notes?

How would psychologists and psychiatrists handle this? (I don't think they would be so direct in revealing that their patients have bipolar disorders, borderline personality disorders, delusion, or other conditions like that, right?)

As of now, we have already responded to her saying that we will directly fax the documentation to her provider per her request, and we will not email her the notes because it is not HIPAA compliant. So I have bought some time to ask for guidance. Thanks in advance for your response! ðŸ™

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Thanks for the input. 
My boss and I feel like this was very likely a manipulative behavior of seeking attention in a negative way, as I actually cut her off per her expression even though she didnâ€™t truly want to be cut off. But just wanted to be prepared for any development. 

Iâ€™m aware of the patients rights to request documentation. And normally I would just give them. Like some of you said, this one was tricky. 
If she still wants the notes for herself, weâ€™ll ask her to pay for printing, processing and shipping, while offering faxing to her provider by request for free. 

I did my best to fill up the details and even had to make some addendums. I would never even imagine that a random conversation of our past employeeâ€™s mistake locking us out of the United Healthcare portal (as an example) would be related to her ankle pain, not to mention to document accordingly.

> **Response 2:** Hi Andy! It sounds like you're being VERY thoughtful in this situation, which is good. It is tricky. Tracy is correct, you cannot deny her medical records. I would look through any mention of mental health in your notes and make sure that everything is professional and objective and non-diagnostic and you can always make addendums to justify why mental health was relevant if necessary. If you know she is currently in therapy, you can try and get a release to give her therapist/psychiatrist the medical records so they can be looped in. If you're concerned about how she will handle the notes, you can follow up with her after they are released and you can always call in a wellness check with local police if you are genuinely concerned that this could trigger SI for her. I would document all conversations with supervisors and such about the precautions you're taking, but as long as any mention of her mental health was clinically relevant to your notes as a therapist, then you have nothing to worry about legally.

### Discussion 504: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT]

**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1560618861376007/

For those of you who use Spry EMR, what has your experience been? What do you like/dislike about it?

Considering switching to it.

Thank you all!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** We have been with them for a year and half now, switching from WebPT and its been great. The transition process was excellent. The front office/desk portion is great (scheduling, billing, etc.). We've noticed an increase in revenue since switching as well as higher amounts of patients paying their balances, since they receive a text message and email statement. The ability to save a card on file, like a credit card or HSA card has been great as well. We can just bill the copay to that card at the end of each visit. There are so many great features, that as office manager has made my job so much easier. You can check eligibility and benefits from the EMR directly, reducing the need to use other websites and allowing for increased productivity. Spry has been great, I believe you will be very pleased with them. Customer service is friendly and fast, we typically get a response within minutes.

> **Response 2:** You'll love it. Affordable and yet has all the features we need. We love them. switched from webpt more than a year back and i thank my stars everyday i see those webpt down posts.

Cindy - A cancellation/no show policy should be the same for all patients;  and equally applied across the entire practice.  

How a practice determines compensation for IC (or employees) for "lost revenue" (missed visit) should be separate and distinct from a patient Cancellation/No Show policy.

### Discussion 515: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-03-04 20:00:29 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 0 reactions, 6 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1681291832642042/

**Original Post:**
For those whose staff are paid per treatment (rather than part time/ full time), how many gaps per day/ week/ etc do your staff get paid for.  Do you use a flat number for the day/ week or is it based on total treatments? Just looking for different ways different clinics handle this. 
Thank you!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I've worked as a 1099 contractor as an employee straight commission (50%+). 

I've never been paid for gaps, except when a client late cancels and the employer collects payment anyway. 

However, an employer who desires to retain employees would make every effort to eliminate long gaps and to keep the schedule full. 

I also appreciate not being required to be in the office when I have no clients on the books.

There are some employers who pay an hourly rate for admin/cleaning/etc when  therr are no appointments scheduled.

> **Response 2:** I worked as a contractor and was paid per patient an hourly rate. For the wellness patient there was a 60/40 split. I only got paid if I was seeing a patient.

### Discussion 521: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2023-02-17 15:01:01 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 0 reactions, 6 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1184628465641717/

**Original Post:**
Obviously I will call them, but just so I know what I'm talking about when I do... Do I need all of these for a mobile outpatient practice with me and 1 independent contractor?
(My state does require workers comp)

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** HPSO tends to be more expensive, but to their credit the policy they provided me includes cyber, professional, and general all in one policy. It also has a business owners extension, which I think is the equivalent of your business owners policy (BOP) as well. I don't have any employees so don't have the WC or EPI. So for me just the HPSO policy + umbrella.

> **Response 2:** You do not need work comp unless you have employees and some states only if 2-3 or more employees.

---

### Discussion 531: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-02-12 19:14:50 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 1 reactions, 5 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1665209954250230/

**Original Post:**
This was requested from a former client?

â€œCould we ask for a â€œsuper billsâ€ coded with the accident as the reason for your us needing your specialty?â€

Is this actually a thing?

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** There are icd 10 codes that look at causes. My favorite is attacked by a duck W61.61.  That being said your treatment notes should have the history that shows this.  If the note is already done personally I would not go back and change my documentation.

> **Response 2:** If I'm understanding this correctly, it sounds like they want you to out on the superbill that services are related to an accident?

Superbill only has the icd-10 and cpt codes. Superbills don't justify medical necessity or cause. That's what the treatment note is for.if it is related to an accident then your documentation should indicate that.

### Discussion 555:

> **Response 1:** I have a cancellation policy acknowledgment form they sign with their intake paperwork. I started with a 50% cancellation fee when I started my business 4 yrs ago. I adapted mine from what I googled online and what I receive from my MDs and allied Med when I seek services in my area.

**Original Post:**
What is the difference between hiring an independent contractor and W-2 PRN? With W-2 PRN you arenâ€™t getting benefits, so is workers comp the main difference?

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Work comp, taxes, supplies, and control are all different.

> **Response 2:** You have no obligations to an independent contractor...work comp ins, benefits, taxes. However, for PRN, everything applies except for benefits. I am a PRN at a place and, with the exception of benefits, the employer is responsible for all of the above.

**Original Post:**
Hi everyone. I received a pre-payment review for 3 dates of service on a patient from Medicare (Pt has Railroad Medicare). Has anyone ever had to do one of these? I keep detailed visit notes, but they want all except for the blood of my first born child ðŸ™„. Do you suggest I type something up on word that addresses all of these requirements along with my treatment note so the auditor can read it more easily? Any suggestions are welcome! Thank you!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Yes, I just went through this and passed/ was paid in full. I provided what they requested (which ultimately was only eval, signed plan of care, daily notes, and progress update as my documentation was adequate to demonstrate medical necessity). I did not send anything extra!

> **Response 2:** #Compliance #RailroadMedicare Palmetto, the MAC for RR Medicare has initiated a series of "Targeted Probe & Educate" reviews (audits) involving outpatient therapy. 

Suggest reviewing letter very carefully to gather all the items required, and address every item in the documentation request. Palmetto provided education on TPE response in a recent presentation. 

Reach out if you need further information or clarification.

### Discussion 593: 

**Date:** 2023-02-06 19:13:45 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 1 reactions, 4 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1176463026458261/

**Original Post:**
Has anyone hired a company to work on their SEO or marketing?  Did you have to do a 1099 for their business?  Thanks!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Itâ€™s very possible you can 1099 them, and should if you can so that way you donâ€™t have to pay employee taxes. But ask your tax preparer first! I wanted to 1099 my PRN providers but I was told I definitely could not in my state and have to W2 them.

> **Response 2:** I do SEO and if you pay thru a cc processor you do not need to do a 1099, as that income is reported by the processor. If they are a corporation you never need to. If LLC, partnership, or sole proprietor then you might if you paid via check, transfer, or cash and total was over $600. I'd dbl check with your accountant to be 100% sure.

### Discussion 609: 

**Date:** 2023-11-08 11:00:39 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 0 reactions, 4 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1351466102291285/

**Original Post:**
Hellonote users- When you are doing a re-certification and are planning to bill a re-eval do you use the "re=certification" note type and just bill part of it as a re-eval;  or do you use the "re-evaluation" note type?? Thanks in advance! Cross posted.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Hey friend! So if you are doing a re-cert to extend the plan of care past the original expiration date (because I'm assuming they are making progress), then you do not bill for a re-evaluation. You can bill for ther act or self care or whatever you think the session would fall under. A re-eval should only be billed if you are re-doing the whole plan of care because there has been a significant change in status, such as a new diagnosis or a hospitalization for something. Re-eval charges are hardly ever billed. Hope that makes sense!

> **Response 2:** I've always done recertification note then billed for whatever I did. I guess depends why you're doing a re-eval. But the recert should work. Idk what the re-eval note type looks like as I've never used it

I have 8 1099's who are treated as such. I am bringing on a W2. I know this means I need to get WC insurance (in Maryland) but I'm confused on the need for group malpractice. My 1099s each have their own malpractice and general liability, and I also have my own. My practice is "additional insured" on each policy. 

Can the W2 get his own and then I reimburse him as "accountable plan" to avoid him being taxed on the reimbursement?

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** No.  W2 all need to be under your policy.  Even if they had their own private policy. That would not legally excuse you from having them under yours.  

Curious why everyone else a 1099 and then take on a W2?

### Discussion 627: 

**Date:** 2023-06-26 18:09:27 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 2 reactions, 3 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1269411230496773/

**Original Post:**
Hey all!

Looking for some advice/creative solutions. 
I left my job in March to pursue my own practice/escape the burnout and get my life in order. I am primarily doing cash concierge ortho/personal training but, I do have a small location that I can practice out of.  A few things happened at the beginning that have made this current venture not sustainable or, not headed in the direction of the dream, without serious overhaul. 

My mentor/past professor is opening up a clinic inside a brand new fighterâ€™s gym and would like me to run it. Initially I would be the only PT but as we expand I will move into the clinical director role. I donâ€™t have specifics yet but this is someone I trust who is building a package for me to make me an offer â€œtoo good to refuseâ€ (high salary, benefits, revenue sharing) 

Since working for myself I have noticed that the â€œperkâ€ I value the most is the freedom/flexibility of schedule. It has allowed me to stay on top of my personal appointments, manage the home, take better care of my dog and enjoy life. Going back to a 9-5 (probably more with the admin side) is where I will have the most trouble adjustingâ€¦ Looking for creative options/perks/benefits that I could suggest in order to make the work life balance more balanced! Iâ€™m willing to compromise on pay or other benefits if it enables a more â€œfreeâ€ life. 

Thanks in advance for any suggestions or ideas!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I would ask what the goal metrics are and what the professor is bringing to the table...do they already have referral sources ready to give you patients? How busy will you need to be in order to have all the great perks/pay? Ask how many visits that person is expecting you to see/when would another clinician be brought on? Once you know numbers, you'll know how busy each day you'll end up being and then you can see how the work life balance will be.

Side thought, if you already have your own business but struggling with getting it going, why not partner with this person instead of being an employee?? Or contract with this person? Once you are an employee, your control of your day is gone.

> **Response 2:** Bargain in control? 1-2 set admin days where you don't treat and can be work from home? Schedule your MD visits a few weeks in advance,and just be allowed to move your schedule around to accommodate? May be harder at the beginning when it's just you. Not easy necessarily but if that's what matters to you, then find a way to make it work

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Our EMR has an online scheduling portal that we've linked to all of our social media. ### Discussion 638: 

**Date:** 2025-04-05 20:10:36 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 1 reactions, 3 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1708932106544681/

**Original Post:**
When transitioning a patient from PT to wellness do you document an initial assessment on day one of wellness? Patients direct access has expired and he still want to work of strength and endurance to prevent reoccurrence of LBP. Please let me know what your protocol is and what documentation you do. TIA

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I indicate in the last PT note that the patient will be transitioning to wellness with an explanation as to why. For wellness documentation is minimum. List exercises and any pertinent info. No true need objective tests/measures or a PT assessment.

Also, wellness does not qualify for insurance reimbursement. 

I have a separate set of paperwork that the patient completes indicating that they understand they will be participating in wellness and that it is not eligible for a superbill because it does not qualify for reimbursement.

### Discussion 647: [MEDIUM ENGAGEMENT] 

**Date:** 2025-02-20 17:26:14 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 7 reactions, 0 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1671435006961058/

**Original Post:**
Sharing a shining example of how to hand off a discussion with a client lead to another member of your team: 

"Only thing I will deal with is the pricing and payment.  He will cover everything else for youðŸ˜Š.  He's real good at what he does.  I trust him completely in my absence"

Had this sent to me from the wedding DJ I'd been primarily communicating with. He turned me over to his colleague, and I was seriously encouraged by how he did it.

Made me confident that this wasn't some new person on the team he didn't trust to do the job alone yet.

Could logic have led me to that same conclusion if he hadn't expressed his full confidence in this individual? Maybe. 

But when the person on the other end places high importance on the decision, there's a lot of emotion involved, too. Don't bet their trust in you.

---

### Discussion 651: 

**Date:** 2023-04-03 22:21:22 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 3 reactions, 2 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1215296729241557/

**Original Post:**
Hello all! I need some help with my very first workshop. I never been to one myself so really I have nothing to go off. I have searched youtube for some examples but they all seem boring... So I am hoping for some good tips and examples.

Do you have any good resources to use? What worked in your case?

Workshop will be on knee pain. Population: active adults. I plan to briefly go over anatomy. Reasons why we have knee pain and do little deeper dive into muscular reasons. Weak quad, weak hips etc...

For "challenge" I plan to ask the group to do SL squat, SL stance (to check ankle stability) and standing quad stretch (heel to butt chick).  Any other/better suggestions?

Lastly, I plan to tech group few exercises to make sure they have strong hips and knees.
-tke with TB (can be combined in squat)
- hip abd like fire hydrants
- sit to stand (BLE, and ULE for stronger folks)
- bridges (BLE, and ULE for stronger)

Thank you!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I've done a ton of workshops. We go over anatomy, common causes and try and find someone we think may do well with a 5-minute treatment miracle. Keep it simple, easy terms, give practical things they can go home with. Happy to chat. DM me

> **Response 2:** Check out MMOA.  Modern Management of the Older Adult.  The have very good resources for several  workshops!

### Discussion 652: 

**Date:** 2022-05-19 16:02:44 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 1 reactions, 3 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/970535040384395/

**Original Post:**
How would one go about bringing on a 1099 employee. And how do you know if you need a 1099 vs full time?

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** 1099s are useful for short duration coverage such as vacation and other types of leave. If you begin to give them their own caseload you will want to W2 them. They do not need to be full time to be a W2 employee. Itâ€™s slightly more money up front but you are protecting your investment on the back end. It is illegal to make a 1099 sign a non compete. This means they could open a practice while working for you, it is actually expected they do this. They cannot take your clients but they can take any referrals of your clients.

> **Response 2:** If you have a small business development center in your area they are an excellent source to get information about contract vs employee.

---

If they arenâ€™t meeting certain expectations, I would discuss that after asking how they are doing.

### Discussion 689: 

**Date:** 2024-11-12 02:55:29 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 0 reactions, 3 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1598178447620048/

**Original Post:**
Not strictly in line with this groups motive, but I was hoping to get some feedback! I am set to potentially move up within my companyâ€™s structure from assistant director to director as our current director/regional partner is moving to a different clinic. Iâ€™m meeting with the president and CEO this week. 

How might you advise structuring this conversation? I donâ€™t want to outright ask for the silver spoon/raise but I donâ€™t want to be told to â€œearn it/prove itâ€ without any objective goals/benchmarks or timelines to achieve. Advice?!

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** How many staff will you be over? Not sure the size of you company but if itâ€™s over multiple clinics and 20+ clinicians then itâ€™s likely you are competing against other managers and external candidates. Seek to solve their problems and show how you have delivered in the past. If itâ€™s just a clinic manager role then yeah you likely have no competition or minimal competition. People move states for regional jobs at big companies

> **Response 2:** Ask about the KPIs going to director. You're equally wondering if it's a good fit for you/your life as they will equally need to fill the role. With a title change like that and added/changed responsibilities there is an expectation of a raise. If the raise or lack thereof (if I'm reading your post right) doesn't align to the increased load it should be a no for you and they will now be required to hire, train, move someone (takes time and money). 

You are in a great position here (not them) remember that.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** they need to fill out w4, you will need to send in new hire for to State.  also, cover them for wc and MD unemployment, CAQH if you bill insurance.  also add them to disability/health ins./ set up 401k if you offer that.

> **Response 2:** WC IS required in MD.  by having them  fill  out the w4 and signi it, the new therapist is a w2 not 1099 employee.

### Discussion 700: 

**Date:** 2022-06-29 12:34:23 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 0 reactions, 3 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/999341204170445/

**Original Post:**
I've had a Medicare question posed to me. In outpatient, for Medicare patients, per Medicare, does the supervising OT have to be in the building when the OTA is treating? Did that loosen for Covid and now will revert back for 2023?
I remember some weird supervision thing but I thought that was supervision of students treating Medicare patients.
(apologies, I may cross post in other groups )

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** #Supervision requirements are noted in IOM 100-02, Ch. 15, Â§230.2(c)  Go To The Source

"General supervision is required for OTAs in all settings except private practice (which requires direct supervision) unless state practice requirements are more stringent, in which case state or local requirements must be followed."

Supervision requirements have been relaxed during the PHE wherein direct supervision could be accomplished using real-time, interactive audio ...... [see further clarification on "how".  This variance on direct supervision is through the later of 12/31/2021 or end of year PHE ends.  If PHE ends this year, supervision would revert back to "in the office suite" for private practice. 

For Rehab Agency, CORF, hospitals, SNFs, and HHA, the supervision remains at "general" supervision.

> **Response 1:** I use PTEverywhere and it has everything I need and I added a fax line which has been handy, but it is pricey. Once I got the hang of things I felt like I could have used a cheaper platform, but uploading videos of myself explaining topics for lengthier education pieces or things I want them to view and videos of myself doing exercises is easy. This is kind of quirky, but I actually picked it over Jane because I liked that PT was in the title and how that seemed professionally, but Jane probably uploads your logo like they do and it's not really an issue, just a preference over here. Once PTEverywhere got pricier, I was busier so it wasn't really an issue and I considered switching but that seemed like a hassle and not worth the reduced price.

### Discussion 715: 

**Date:** 2022-08-31 14:17:29 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools

**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1044330936338138/

**Original Post:**
Can anyone please share a template of a cancelation notice they have patients sign? (Something specifying fee for canceling under 24hs and not showing)

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** CANCELLATION POLICY
I understand that all appointments must be canceled a minimum of 24 hours before the scheduled appointment start time. I understand that cancellations made inside of this 24-hour cancellation window will be charged the full session rate. I understand that if I arrive late for my scheduled appointment, the session will be limited to the remaining scheduled time, and I will be charged the full session rate.

This is a bullet that they initial in my one page consent/financial agreement page.

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** I believe you're in CA...we can't hire 1099 due to Assembly Bill 5 (the Uber rule) unless it is a business to business. Probably a good time to network with another business in the area that you can pay a flat rate per session. Otherwise you could hire a PRN employee

> **Response 2:** If you are just hiring for your specific vacation period a 1099 might be appropriate. If you are going to use PRN for other times etc I would consider PRN employee.

As either a solo clinician or maybe even part of a small team, would there be any interest or profit to be made (in your opinion) if there was a web based platform that would allow you to:

Utilize skeletal tracking for exercise based games (to boost patient engagement and active participation in their recovery)

Have AI provide a post session score based on patient performances relative to the exercise video they are mimicking (can be synchronous or asynchronous). Can compare scores session over session to assess progress.

Exercise based games is the most advanced thing in the list here. That is the only thing that has genuinely stood out to me so far. ðŸ‘ðŸ‘ðŸ‘ðŸ‘ Curious on equipment needed though.

Patient performance score relative to a video sounds like a terrible idea. There are so many ways to move, and not every human is built the same way. Asking them to chase a score for how well they match someone else sounds counterproductive to encouraging them to move their OWN body better.ðŸ‘ŽðŸ‘ŽðŸ‘ŽðŸ‘Ž

AI generated SOAP note is great. Would be concerned about training the AI.

I'm not familiar with monthly license prices. Assuming that's like a subscription service, I'd expect to see something like this marketed at $200ish per month? Or per user? I really don't know. That price feels low, possibly. It would depend on how some of the features shake out.

> **Response 1:** Yo answer question specifically For DN. They would need to sign a consent form prior. Make sure you sanitize the area and Carry a sharps container.

> **Response 2:** Check with your state practice act. I think some vary slightly but most require a signed informed consent prior to txt, certain amount of experience may be required, and I think some require screening the patient prior to txt. My attorney said she had a PT client lose her license because she didnâ€™t screen prior to needling B UT and patient ended up with a pneumothorax. The state (not sure which state) took license away because no screen was performed despite documentation for proper needling technique and needle placement. My state doesnâ€™t require a screen but I do a quick one anyway now. She advised good documentation of the signed informed consent, screening, for needles used/how many, muscles treated, and response to tx. 

Hope this helps!

### Discussion 748: 

**Date:** 2024-02-01 13:57:36 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 4 reactions, 0 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1404230440348184/

**Original Post:**
TLDR: Don't forget to make sure you have DMARC, DKIM, and SPF setup on your domain DNS (where your URL is hosted). This not only applies for ppl using third parties to send newsletters, etc but also when using any branded email address. These are to prevent email spoofing and verify the senders are who they say they are. Those who don't have them can now encounter deliverability issues as of Feb 2024.

Here's a little bit about it from constant contact: https://knowledgebase.constantcontact.com/email-digital-marketing/articles/KnowledgeBase/7644-What-is-DMARC?lang=en_US

This first started as being for accounts who send 5000 emails per day, however most emails clients are now making it highly recommended or even required. You might see an alert popup up on logging in, don't ignore it.

If you don't add these, constant contact is just one that will change your sender address to one of theirs until you do. 

Here's what these things are in a nutshell:

Imagine you're at a costume party where everyone wears a mask, making it tough to tell who's who. This situation is a bit like the internet's email system: it's easy for someone to disguise themselves as someone else and send you emails pretending to be your bank, your friend, or your boss. That's where DMARC, DKIM, and SPF step in, acting as the party's bouncers, verifying the identity of each guest.

SPF (Sender Policy Framework) is like a guest list at the party entrance. It checks if the sender's email server is on the list of approved servers for that domain. If the server isn't on the list, SPF tells the email system, "This one's trying to crash the party!" and can prevent the email from reaching your inbox.

DKIM (DomainKeys Identified Mail) is like a secret handshake. It uses a digital signature attached to the email, ensuring that the message really comes from where it says it does and hasn't been tampered with along the way. Think of it as checking if a guest knows the secret handshake before letting them mingle.

DMARC (Domain-based Message Authentication, Reporting, and Conformance) watches over SPF and DKIM like a head bouncer. It uses the results from both to decide what to do with an email that fails the checks. DMARC can tell the email system to do nothing, quarantine the email, or reject it outright. It also sends reports back, saying who tried to get in, so the party planners can adjust their guest list and handshake as needed.

These three work together to make sure that the only emails reaching your inbox are from the people who they claim to be from, keeping the party crashers out and making the email world a safer place to communicate.

Happy to answer any questions or drop links to instructions for any hosts below.

---

### Discussion 810: 

**Date:** 2025-07-01 14:36:28 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 2 reactions, 0 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1779154179522473/

**Original Post:**
I posted a while back about my progress on developing my own automation within Google Workspace as an EMR. 

I finally completed the automatic mileage tracker. Now I get an email with a Google Form link at the end of each day I see clients. After I fill out the Form it logs my miles for all clients and formats it into a Google Sheet for easy viewing and tracking. Iâ€™ll test this for the remainder of the year and then plan to implement it at the beginning of next year just to give ample time for troubleshooting. 

I started a project that will support the mileage tracker and make scheduling easier as well. I typically schedule people at set times on set days, so my schedule is consistent. So it will allow me to choose the client I am scheduling for, set the start day of the visits, set the days of the week they will occur, set the times for each specific day, and set the number of visits to schedule. Then it will add me and the client as attendees of the visit and set the location as their address, which will allow the mileage tracker to do its thing. I will also be adding a feature for scheduling evals that will allow me to create new contacts and schedule their eval at the same time. In addition, it will have a feature for creating vacation time. Vacation time will be set as â€œbusyâ€ and when visits are being scheduled using this app it will look for vacation time and schedule around it as blocked out time. 

The upfront time for developing these isnâ€™t insignificant, but for a solo practitioner it is well worth it to save the money I do not using a traditional EMR.

### Discussion 831: 

**Date:** 2023-07-27 16:18:42 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 2 reactions, 0 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1288688675235695/

**Original Post:**
If you work with any insurance companies and aren't implementing RTM into your practice, you're missing out on thousands of dollars of extra income per year that is 99% passive with the correct software once you setup the workflow in your system.

I've been utilizing SaRa Health https://www.sarahealth.io/ for RTM and I cannot say enough good things about their software and development team working with them has been an absolute breeze. It is completely hands off once you take the 30 seconds to setup the patient in the system. They take everything from their from messaging the patient and even tell you what to document in your note and what codes to bill. They notify you when to check in with a patient if a response is "abnormal" and give me a summary of responses over the past month.

This is a must with any practice that bills Medicare and private insurance.

### Discussion 857: 

**Date:** 2024-03-29 10:15:56 | **Topic:** 06-staffing-hiring-team
**Engagement:** 0 reactions, 1 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1439984950106066/

**Original Post:**
Received a job offer to be a home health OT as an independent contractor, which I have not been before. This company typically provides aide and nursing services, and is just starting up providing therapies. of course I would be having my own liability insurance, but what would be the other risks involved with signing on to a company that is so new to offering therapies? Feeling a little overwhelmed and hesitant to sign the contract

**Community Responses:**

> **Response 1:** Risks would include them limiting how many visits you could do or ending the contract when they are unsuccessful at implementing the knew program. Make sure they are paying you enough if you are 1099. You should be getting 20% more as a 1099 compared to w2. Also, use it as am opportunity to build your business. Make sure they will let you hire COTAs through your business which is contracted with them so they can do some of your visits for you. Then go out and find more contracts like that. 
Oh and make sure they contract your LLC, not you directly. 
Shoot me a message if you want to discuss it further.

### Discussion 952: 

**Date:** 2023-01-08 23:43:20 | **Topic:** 05-operations-systems-tools
**Engagement:** 0 reactions, 0 comments
**Source:** https://www.facebook.com/groups/uncagedcliniciangroup/permalink/1154654331972464/

**Original Post:**
Is the solo practice era coming to an end?
There are fear that the solo practitioner will be a rare, or thing of the past. True as that my seem; especially to those whose income and business model is married to third-party payers, there is also a growing part of healthcare clinicians may be ignoring. It is the cash-paying patient. OK, before you dismiss me, hear me out! Most insured Americans have high deductibles, making them cash patients up to 6 or 12k (whatever their deductible is). In addition, a growing part of the population is without insurance. Combined, these two groups make up 51% of Americans. So, why are we bothering to fight with insurance companies when most patients cannot use it even when they have it? Because we have always looked to insurance companies to tell us what we are worth.
Here is the problem with processing insurance for patients with high deductibles. The overhead goes up by multiples whenever insurance companies have to put their blessing on your claim. Insurance is essential; however, it is now only for catastrophic events. Recurring healthcare should be cash-based.
That brings us to the how? How do you start a cash practice? Several platforms on the market can help. Because I am a clinician and a software engineer, I created a marketplace that allows all the providers and me on the platform to state what they charge and the insurances they accept. In turn, I drive patients to the platform, and they get to choose a provider based on price, insurance accepted, distance from the provider, reputation rating, etc. The platform takes the provider to the discomfort of negotiating prices with patients. Furthermore, when the patients book appointments, they pay online, so I do not have to employ an army of people to collect my money. All the providers on Hutano have told me they love how the idea of a marketplace like this saves time and money.
Overhead is a real issue in healthcare. And it comes in two flavors, fixed and variable. Fixed overhead may be what it is. Meaning there is little you can do about it. Variable overhead, on the other hand, you can manage with technology.
I hear healthcare is complicated more often than I can count. But is it that different from other industries? Actually, not really! Consider this; there are five essential steps to accessing and providing primary healthcare. Finding a healthcare provider, booking an appointment, completing paperwork, receiving care, and follow-up care. If we figure out how to create technology that addresses the inefficiencies in each step, we will have fixed healthcare - at least primary care.
Traditionally, healthcare tends to mesh many technologies together and hope everything will work out. Inevitably we solve upstream problems without applying any thought to the downstream issues.
Let me give an example. Suppose you use  Zoc Doc to automate and manage scheduling. Great! Your patients find you and book appointments efficiently. However, your waiting room is still packed with patients filling out paperwork. And yes! your patients still wait 45 minutes plus to receive care. At the end of the day, you are overwhelmed despite the efficient scheduling. So what is the solution?
Software should make our lives more efficient. Unfortunately, no software on the market addresses the inefficiencies in each of the five steps. Practice management software should make finding providers and booking appointments as simple as Zoc Doc. Furthermore, patients should be able to fill out the intake, attach pertinent medical documents like imaging and lab reports, then pay for medical services online. By the time a patient walks into the clinic, the provider should be armed with all they need to diagnose and treat. But why stop there? The information a patient just entered into their intake could transfer automatically into the HPI portion of the encounter note. That way, by the time a provider starts writing a note, the patient has filled out the chief complaint, medical and social histories, medication list, preferred pharmacy, and even their vitals if that is something they can do at home. So the clinician's time can be more effectively spent interpreting the objective measures in your tests and measures, assigning a diagnosis and treatment plan. It would be great if follow-up appointments were set up in the EMR and sent directly to the patient's phone. Lastly, it would be great for any outside referrals to be managed directly in the EMR, sending referrals directly to other clinicians with access to treatment notes upon acceptance or referral.
My point is that technology saves time and money because; and clinicians will not need to employ people to schedule and manage appointments. Instead, like an airline, patients can book and manage their appointments.
I created a platform three years ago that does what I just shared with you. Twelve other providers and I are on the Hutano platform, and the results have been encouraging. And, as a solo, cash-based practitioner, my time is no longer bogged down with administrative tasks. So, please visit us at Hutano.com to set up your free account, and let me know how I can help your practice be more efficient.
As a software engineer and clinician, I consult with other clinicians. Please let me know if I can be a resource for your practice. Ephraim Makuve, PT, DPT, MBA HA. www.hutano.com | also available on the Appstore and Google Play Store

---

Licensed in PA.
